France Does Not Want to Return the Saar Region Before 1935

(Paris) - Hitler recently expressed the opinion that the Saar region should be returned to Germany unconditionally. The French House of Representatives Foreign Affairs Committee held a meeting on this matter, chaired by Herriot, and passed a resolution, advocating that the return of the region should not be considered before the 1935 referendum. A press release was then issued, stating that the purpose of this resolution was to make the government pay attention to the need to consult with the League of Nations to protect treaty rights and the complete freedom of the referendum. According to the treaty, voters must have been residing in the Saar region since 1919 and be at least 20 years old, while Germans who have moved to the region since that year are not allowed to express their opinions. When the court makes a decision, spectators are prohibited, but the law does not provide for the elimination of the reproductive function of those who are abnormal in sexual matters. (New York) After being criticized for his recent attacks on the US President's monetary policy, Smith, a prominent figure in the US Democratic Party, wrote an article in the magazine "New Outlook," which he edits, attacking the government's relief, economic, and monetary policies. He claimed that if the desire is to have more public works projects underway by February 15th of next year, the Public Works Administration must be completely reorganized immediately. He also pointed out that the government's newly established Civil Works Administration, intended to accommodate four million unemployed workers this winter, is merely an attempt to cover up the failures of the Public Works Administration. He criticized the cumbersome and inconvenient organization of the Public Works Administration, describing it as top-heavy, inefficient in its paperwork and meetings, and lacking effectiveness in implementation. In addition, he listed the government's New Deal agencies such as AAA (Agricultural Adjustment Administration), NRA (National Recovery Administration), PWA (Public Works Administration), CWA (Civil Works Administration), FCA (Farm Credit Administration), RFC (Reconstruction Finance Corporation), and other agencies, mocking the government by saying it resembles heartless professors in the government, playing word puzzle games with inverted letters. (National Telegraph, 30th)

(Washington) Following Smith's attack on the government, Secretary of the Interior Ickes today criticized him for becoming increasingly resentful due to unfulfilled ambitions and disappointment, causing his judgment to be obscured by his hatred of the government. Speaker of the House Rayburn also stated that if Smith does not want to join the ranks of reconstruction, then he is free not to join, which will not hinder the progress of the ranks. In addition, Father Coughlin of Detroit, who had previously criticized Smith's attack on the government's monetary policy as being influenced by loans from banker Morgan, reiterated his statement in Detroit yesterday after Smith issued a clarification. (National Telegraph, 3rd)

Pro-Silver Faction Activities

(New York) With the end of the US Congressional recess approaching and the date for reconvening in January of next year drawing near, the activities of those advocating for the remonetization of silver are intensifying day by day. Senator Borah, former Chairman of the Senate Foreign Relations Committee, who has been relatively inactive since the Congressional recess this spring, is now launching a new silver movement and is about to become one of the leaders of the pro-silver faction. (Havas, 30th)

U.S. Fears Soviet Competition in International Petroleum Trade

(Washington) The United States' recognition of the Soviet Union has sparked speculation among the national petroleum industry about the future impact on international petroleum trade. The United States accounts for the first largest oil production in the world, and the Soviet Union the second, with the two countries accounting for 72% of the world's oil production. If they can act jointly, it will have a significant impact on future efforts to stabilize the world oil market. However, it is expected that after the resumption of diplomatic relations between the Soviet Union and the United States, the Soviet Union will resume purchasing oil exploration and refining machinery from the United States, increase its oil production, and aggressively promote sales in the Far East and South America, leading to fierce competition with American oil. (National Telegraph, 30th)

Completion Ceremony for the Martyrs' Shrine Built by Feng in Mount Tai; Feng Personally Presided over the Ceremony

(Jinan) The Martyrs' Shrine built by Feng in Mount Tai, near the Five Worthies Shrine in Puzhao Temple, has excellent scenery. The completion ceremony was held at 9 a.m. today. Feng personally presided over the ceremony and led the attendees in paying respects. He had personally witnessed the shrine in Luanzhou during the Northern Expedition. There are martyrs' shrines in various places, but the north is the only place without one. I built this shrine to comfort their spirits and to commemorate the martyrs in order to inspire future generations. Zheng Jicheng delivered a thank-you speech on behalf of the families of the martyrs. Zhou Bai, the magistrate of Taian County, spoke, saying that Feng had economized on food and clothing to build the martyrs' shrine. The martyrs in the shrine include Guo Songling and his wife, Zhang Shaocheng, Zheng Jinsheng, and the martyrs who died in Luanzhou, Wang Jinyu, etc. (Special Dispatch, 1st)

Yang Shukan and Others Request Cancellation of Additional Tax on Sichuan Salt Sold to Guangdong

(Nanjing) Members of the Central Committee Yang Shukan, Xie Chi, and Huang Fusheng, among others, sent a telegram to the Central Government on the 29th regarding the additional tax on Sichuan salt sold to Hubei, requesting the withdrawal of the order. The original telegram stated that the Sichuan Salt Guilds of Shashi and Yichang, as well as the Sichuan salt representatives, reported that according to the General Office's telegram, an additional tax of $1.50 per dan has been added to Sichuan salt transported to western Hubei and northern Chu, bringing the total tax on Sichuan salt to as much as nine yuan per dan, which is already a heavy burden. If the tax is further increased, it may be unbearable. Moreover, China's salt tax has always been differentiated, considering the weight of the salt capital to determine the level of tax, to adjust its fairness. Now, the tax on sales to Hubei and Chu is uniquely increased, making it even heavier and more difficult to bear. Salt is a daily necessity and is different from other consumer luxury goods. Please consider the suffering of the people of Sichuan and Chu, who have repeatedly suffered from floods, bandits, wars, and earthquakes, and have nowhere to turn, and grant the withdrawal of the order to eliminate the source of chaos and quell the disputes. Please also send a telegram to that effect. (Special Dispatch, 1st)

Ministry of Finance Currently Planning Estate Tax Law; Investigation Work Quite Tricky

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Finance has ordered the Tax Bureau to draft a plan for the implementation of an estate tax. Minister Kong stated that the estate tax is one of the best sources of tax revenue, and most countries in the world have already implemented it. In this time of financial difficulty in our country, we should naturally also implement an estate tax. The Ministry is currently planning the estate tax law. After it is passed by the Central Government, it will be sent to the Legislative Yuan to instruct the Financial Committee of the Yuan to study and draft it. According to foreign advisors, the prerequisite for the estate tax is to adjust the census and investigate the people's actual property. Because in recent years, those with strong capital mostly reside in Shanghai and deposit their money in foreign banks, the investigation work is quite tricky. (Special Dispatch, 1st)

Rescue of the Cotton Yarn and Textile Industry Under Consideration

(Nanjing) The issue of government assistance for the cotton yarn and textile industry was submitted to the Rural Reconstruction Commission by the Ministries of Finance and Industry, and it was decided that the government should negotiate with government-run banks to provide a low-interest loan of 20 million yuan for assistance. This has been delayed until now and has not yet been completed. It has recently been heard that the plan has been returned to the National Economic Council and the Cotton Industry Control Committee for unified handling. According to Liu Yinqin, a member of the committee, the Cotton Industry Control Committee is still planning to allocate 20 million yuan to assist the cotton yarn and textile industry. However, the reasons for the decline of each cotton mill are different, and in-depth research is needed before assistance can be provided. Otherwise, if the root cause is not removed, temporary maintenance will have no hope of development in the future. Fundamental improvements are necessary for any effective result. At present, all measures are still under consideration, and Chen Guangfu is responsible for raising funds. It is also planned that, under the guidance of the Control Committee, the factories will jointly form a joint cotton yarn sales organization in Shanghai to avoid jealousy among the industry. (Special Dispatch, 1st)

Ministry of Finance Investigates Reed Salt and Native Niter

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Finance instructed the Changlu Salt Transportation Envoy that there are two types of native niter produced in the area, land-produced and sea-produced. According to a previous report from the Jingqian Transportation Envoy, beach-produced niter is currently managed by the Niter Bureau. The Ministry requested instructions on whether land-produced native niter should be allowed to be manufactured and sold. After investigation, there are three types of land-produced native niter in chemistry: one is potassium nitrate, which is gunpowder; the second is sodium nitrate, which is Chilean nitrate, which can be used as a raw material for gunpowder and belongs to the scope of niter mines, which should be strictly managed by the Niter Mine Bureau; the third is sodium sulfate, which is refined land niter and is mirabilite, which is currently not managed. However, beach-produced sea niter is also sodium sulfate and is currently managed by the Niter Bureau. The actual annual production of sodium sulfate, one type of land-produced native niter, in the area, and whether it has any relationship with salt affairs and niter affairs, and whether it should be managed in the same way as sea-produced native niter, should be carefully investigated by the transportation envoy for approval. (Special Dispatch, 1st)

The disciplinary actions in sections two to four of the preceding paragraph do not apply to elected political officials, legislators, or members of the Control Yuan. After the Fujian Incident, Chairman Chiang Still Pays Attention to Bandit Suppression; Armies in Eastern Jiangxi Still Follow Original Plans

Nanchang Correspondence: The Fujian Incident has now moved towards a military resolution. The eastern part of Jiangxi has the longest border with Fujian. However, the border area which connects Tingzhou, Liancheng Jianning, Ninghua, Guangze, Shaowu, Chong'an, Ruijin, Guangchang, Nanfeng, Nancheng, Lichuan, Zixi, Qianshan and other counties are all occupied by bandits and deeply radicalized. The Fujian side used it as a barrier, but although there are hundreds of thousands of central army troops in eastern Jiangxi, they were unable to directly attack due to not wanting to harm the citizens. Therefore, the armies in eastern Jiangxi still follow their original plan of suppressing the bandits. Moreover, in recent days, due to the urgent situation in Fujian and Zhejiang, the bandits thought that there was an opportunity to take advantage of it and tried to advance from Jinxi towards Fuzhou and Dongxiang in the north. Chiang saw this as a good opportunity to quickly eliminate the bandits, so he personally directed everything. At the same time, he ordered the Provincial Government to strictly enforce the 40-odd counties along the Fuhe and Jianhe rivers in Jiangxi, requiring them to complete the blockhouse projects in counties, cities, towns, and traffic arteries within a month to strengthen defenses and prevent any loopholes. Chiang is extremely busy working in Fuzhou. Important figures such as Chen Zhaoying, Zhang Zhenlin Zhiyuan, and Lu Xingrong, who came to the province for instructions, took the Jiangxi-Fujian Road bus to Fuzhou to visit Chiang. Rumors that Chiang will go to Nanjing or Zhejiang are inaccurate. (November 29th)

He Gonggan Assumes the Position of Fujian Provincial Governor; All Provincial Agencies Undergo Organizational Changes; Educational Funding Fundamentally Shaken

Fuzhou Correspondence: After He Gonggan was appointed Governor of Fujian Province by the People's Government, he took office on the 25th in the old Provincial Government Auditorium. There was initially a proposal to divide Fujian Province into two or three provinces, but this has been cancelled. The provincial system is currently being drafted by He. As for its organization, it has been decided to abolish the two departments and establish sections, a total of five sections. The selection of section chiefs has been approved by He. Ruan Shuqing was appointed as Secretary-General and concurrently as the head of the Civil Affairs Section, Qian Luzhou (i.e., Qian Zongqi) was appointed as the head of the General Affairs Section, Li Ruozhu was appointed as the head of the Education Section, Liu Mianyi (i.e., Liu Pinye) was appointed as the head of the Economic Section, and Li Bo was appointed as the head of the Finance Section. On the 26th, the new provincial government began to operate, with its office located at the former site of the Department of Civil Affairs. Among the five section chiefs, only Qian Luzhou was unable to come due to illness in Shanghai and was temporarily replaced by Wang Buai. The rest all took office at the same time. The takeover procedures for the various departments are being handled separately these days. In addition to the Department of Civil Affairs, which has already been taken over immediately, the archives of the Department of Education were taken over by Li Ruozhu on the 26th. Its office was changed to the Cultural Committee. The archives of the Department of Construction were not taken over by Liu Mianyi until the 27th. Shanghai Chezhi is the Economic Committee, and the Department of Finance took until the 28th to divide due to the issue of national tax revenue, after He negotiated with Jiang Guangnai, Zha Xiqing, and others. All special taxes belong to the Ministry of Finance, while the rest belongs to the Provincial Government.

The new provincial government has extremely thin regulations. In addition to the governor, who receives 200 yuan per month, the section chiefs receive 80 yuan per month, and the section staff are divided into four grades: 20 yuan, 30 yuan, 40 yuan, and 50 yuan. The new provincial government's facilities and policies have not yet been announced, but it is heard that He Gonggan has ordered the Civil Affairs Section to assess the political achievements of the county chiefs. There will be a round of appointments and removals in the near future.

Regarding the education policy, there has recently been a proposal to abolish ordinary middle schools and replace them with vocational schools. However, educational funding has been fundamentally shaken. The funding for teachers in Fujian Province was originally 120,000 yuan from the salt surtax. Since the recent changes in the situation, the salt affairs in northern Fujian have completely stopped, the salt tax revenue is minimal, and the education has been unable to allocate it. The educational circles sent a letter to He Gonggan and Jiang Guangnai on the 27th, requesting relief. He presented it to the People's Government meeting on the 27th for discussion, and it was decided to hand it over to the Ministry of Finance and the Economic Committee for joint fundraising and relief. He Gonggan talked to the education circle, saying that the educational funding must be guaranteed, but if the salt affairs do not develop, then it will be too difficult to restore the education funding to its original state. (November 30th) (Min Yan She)

Huang Qixiang Has Not Separated from the Third Party; The People's Daily Denies Huang's Telegram Announcing Departure; The People's Revolutionary Grand Alliance Has Not Begun to Organize

Fuzhou Dispatch: After the establishment of the Fujian Provincial People's Government, Jiang Guangnai, Li Guangda, Chen Mingshu, Cai Tingkai, Li Jishen, and others first issued a telegram declaring their separation from the Kuomintang. Subsequently, Shen Guanghan and others also telegraphed their departure from the party a few days later. When Jiang, Cai, and others issued their telegrams, Fuzhou newspapers once published that Huang Qixiang had also telegraphed his separation from the Third Party. It was also heard that the People's Revolutionary Grand Alliance would be established above the government to supervise the administrative organs. Now, according to the Fuzhou People's Daily (formerly the Republic Daily), a special announcement has been published regarding Huang Qixiang's departure from the Second Party, stating that Huang did not send such a telegram, and the People's Revolutionary Grand Alliance has not yet begun to organize. (November 30) (Min Yan News Agency)

Bai Yuhuan Was Assassinated in Tianjin; Bai Usually Vigorously Criticized Party Rule; This Assassination Is Suspected to Have Political Background

Tianjin Dispatch: Last night (around 7 p.m. on the 28th), an assassination case suddenly occurred in Gengyu Lane, Akashi Street, Japanese Concession. The victim was Bai Yuhuan, who resided at No. 2 in the lane. It is reported that the assassins who entered Bai's residence were three young men. Bai was shot three times, all with Browning pistol bullets. After firing the shots, the three men fled in a hurry. The Japanese police station, upon hearing the news, immediately dispatched Japanese police and plainclothes detectives to surround the Akashi Street area and conduct a search. By that time, the assassins had already escaped. Special agents entered Bai's residence to investigate and found that Bai's left arm was injured by three shots. He was immediately carried to Yan Gu Hospital on Naniwa Street for washing and treatment. However, due to Bai's advanced age (58 years old this year), he suffered great damage to his spirit and body from this attack and shock. Bai was from Tianmen County, Hubei Province. In his early years, he ran around to make revolution with Sun Yat-sen, Huang Xing, and others. Later, Sun and Huang disagreed, and Bai joined Huang and others in the same revolutionary cause. After the success of the Northern Expedition, Bai was incompatible with the Kuomintang. In the 18th and 19th years of the Republic, he lived in Japan, publishing the magazine "Republic of China," criticizing party rule with fierce words, and secretly running a party with Chen Jiongming and others, criticizing the Kuomintang. Last year, Bai came to Tianjin with Chen Jiongming to engage in activities and established the Zhen Bao in the Japanese Concession, with Bai as the chief writer. After Chen Jiongming returned to Hong Kong this year, he passed away in Hong Kong. Bai stayed in Tianjin. Because Zhen Bao was banned, it was renamed Zhen Bao, with an editorial department and business department set up on Suma Street. Bai resided at No. 2 Gengyu Lane. Recently, after the Fujian Incident, Bai wrote articles supporting the People's Government. Last night, after dinner at his residence, he was about to go out for a bath when three young men suddenly broke in. Before he could speak, he was attacked and immediately fell to the ground. The perpetrators fled. The Japanese police station is currently investigating the political background of the assassins and actively pursuing the culprits.

According to another report, Bai Yuhuan was the leader of the United Democratic Socialist Party. At 10 a.m. yesterday, two young men in Western suits (both around 24 or 25 years old) broke into Bai's residence, claiming to buy newspapers. Then they went to No. 8 Gengyu Lane to look at the house. Bai's attendants, seeing that the two men looked suspicious, told Bai to prepare for precautions. Unexpectedly, at about 7 p.m. that night, three young men in Western suits suddenly came, each holding a pistol. One of them first restrained the servants downstairs, and the other two went upstairs to search. At that time, Bai was taking a bath and saw two men pointing guns at him. Knowing they were not good people, he jumped up and grabbed the person in front of him. The person behind him shot Bai three times in a row. Bai suffered severe injuries to his chest and arms and bled a lot. The attendants rushed over at the sound, and Bai lay in a pool of blood. The assassins all fled. The Japanese police station sent people to investigate and ordered people to send Bai to the hospital, while trying to detect the culprits. According to the doctor's diagnosis, the injury was too serious, and his life was in great danger. (November 29)

Hubei Provincial People's Congress; Five Proposals Passed on the Spot

Hankou Dispatch: The Hubei Provincial People's Congress was held at the Yue Ma Chang in Wuchang at 9 a.m. on the 30th. Officials from various agencies and organizations, students from various schools, and people from all walks of life, totaling more than 20,000 people, attended the meeting. He Chenjun, Ye Peng, Wang Shiliu, Cheng Qibao, and others were elected to the presidium, with Wang Shiliu as the general chairman. He reported the significance of the meeting. Ye Peng, the representative of the military, Cheng Qibao, the representative of the political circles, Yang Xingqin, the municipal party committee, Lu Jian, the representative of the academic circles, Ai Yuying, the representative of the press, Duan Gongshuang, the representative of the labor circles, and Zhou Zhenyu, the representative of the business circles, successively gave speeches, and then announced the proposals: (1) Declaration of the Congress; (2) Telegraphing the Central Party Department to order the National Government to issue a clear order to punish the rebellious Fujian Province; (3) Telegraphing the whole country to unanimously condemn the rebellious Fujian Province; (4) Warning the 19th Route Army to maintain its past glory, quickly correct the chaos, and eliminate the pseudo-organization; (5) Requesting the military and police organs of this province to strictly investigate and arrest the anti-rebellion elements who are lurking and active. The following is a record of the Central Committee, the General Headquarters, the Pacification Office, and three telegrams to Jiang Guangnai and Cai Tingkai: (1) Telegram to the Central Committee, "To the Central Party Department, In recent years, the country has been plagued by many disasters. Internally, the Red Bandits have been rampant, and externally, strong neighbors have been oppressing us. All Chinese people should be aware of the danger of stacked eggs and strive to help each other with the will to support each other. Sincere unity is needed to save the country from danger. However, Chen Mingshu, Li Jishen, and others, using false names, started chaos in Fujian, recruited all reactionary elements, claiming to be representatives of the masses, and arbitrarily formed a pseudo-government, changing the flag and colluding with the Jiangxi Red Bandits to form a military agreement, colluding with each other. They also flattered and courted Japanese imperialists, secretly colluding with each other, not hesitating to help the bandits to disturb the people and invite foreign bandits to overthrow the capital. Judging from their intentions, they want to use the nation that the martyrs painstakingly created to satisfy their personal desires to seize power. After hearing this, we feel extremely hateful. The people of this province, on November 30, held a people's congress and unanimously decided to appeal to your meeting to instruct the National Government to issue a clear order to launch a large-scale attack to lay the foundation of the country and curb the chaos. The future of the party and the country depends on it. The Hubei People's Congress for Punishing Rebellion Koupian." (2) Telegram to the General Headquarters, the Pacification Office, and the Police Department, "To the Commander-in-Chief of the Suppression of Bandits in the Provinces of Henan, Hubei, and Anhui, the Pacification Commissioner's Office stationed in Hubei, and the Wuhan Garrison Command, Chen Mingshu, Li Jishen, and others have changed the era name, usurped the throne, and betrayed the central government. Their crimes are obvious, and the whole country is indignant. For the sake of upholding justice, the people of this province held a people's congress to punish rebellion at the Yue Ma Chang in Wuchang on November 30 and proposed that the military and police organs of this province strictly investigate and arrest anti-rebellion elements lurking and active in Wuhan. This was unanimously approved by the whole body. Wuhan is an important town on the Yangtze River, and it is inevitable that anti-rebellion elements will lurk and be active. If they are not strictly investigated and arrested, it may hinder public security. In addition to sending telegrams, we hereby send a telegram to earnestly request strict enforcement to pacify the people. Deeply praying, the Hubei People's Congress for Punishing Rebellion respectfully seals the telegram on the 30th of November." (3) Telegram to Jiang Cai, "To Chairman Jiang Guangnai of Fuzhou and Director Cai Tingkai, In recent years, foreign troubles and bandit chaos have been intertwined, and the survival of the country is imminent. All Chinese people should be inspired by nature and conscience and work together to save the situation. However, Chen Mingshu, Li Jishen, and others, disregarding the overall situation, started chaos in Fujian, arbitrarily established names, and organized a government, colluding with the Communist bandits and betraying the party and the country. Their crimes are heinous, and the whole country is indignant. Recalling the telegram of the 19th Route Army withdrawing from Shanghai, it was declared that they would never participate in civil wars. Unexpectedly, this time they abandoned their glorious history and betrayed their past oaths, foolishly providing Chen and other rebels with the opportunity to use them to launch a civil war. When the news came, we were extremely surprised. The people of this province, indignant at Chen Mingshu and others for harming the country and the people, specially held a people's congress to punish rebellion on November 30 and unanimously decided to warn the 19th Route Army to maintain its past glory, quickly correct the chaos, and eliminate the pseudo-organization. This congress, for the sake of cherishing the past reputation of you two gentlemen, does not hesitate to make a final loyal admonition. We deeply hope that you will come to your senses, abide by the intentions of the central government, disband the pseudo-government in Fujian Province, and bring the main rebels to justice. It is not too late to turn back, do not miss the opportunity. This telegram is respectfully delivered, and we hope you will understand. The Hubei People's Congress for Punishing Rebellion respectfully seals the telegram on the 30th of November." (November 30)

Robbery in Xishan Township, Suzhou

At about 10 p.m. on the 30th, more than ten bandits suddenly came to He Yansheng's house in Lujia Village, Xishan Township, Dongting, and robbed them, losing about 200 yuan. He Zidaogen and the long-term worker Zhu were kidnapped. Wuxi Li Tongfeng Mixed and Sold Fake Ginseng and Disputes; Li Tongfeng Ginseng Medicine System in Shuyuan Lane in the City

Li Yunquan, a local, has been running the business for more than ten years with his own funds. The business is normal. This year, in order to attract customers and promote business, he purchased two Taiwanese gray deer (each costing only a few angles per catty) and falsely posed them as Northeast sika deer (with red hair and plum blossom white spots, each costing about eight or nine hundred yuan). In mid-month, he held a deer slaughter ceremony, jointly making nine whole deer. At the same time, he extensively published advertisements in the local newspaper, spreading the word that all kinds of ginseng and medicine sold were at the expense of blood. But the day before yesterday, a man named Chen Yingen from Tangkou bought a package of real American ginseng from the store and found on the spot that it was counterfeit. As a result, a dispute arose, and they twisted each other to the first sub-bureau of public security. After questioning by Officer Qin, he ordered Li Hanxian, a partner of the store, to pay a bail and wait to be sent to the General Bureau for interrogation, and at the same time sent a letter to the Pharmaceutical Association to identify the authenticity for verification. Then, according to the Pharmaceutical Association's reply, Li Hanxian, a partner of the store, claimed that it was a defective product of the store, and it was considered unnecessary to identify it. Then the store hired a lawyer to publish a statement in the newspaper and automatically convened a temporary meeting of the Pharmaceutical Association to identify it, but only seven or eight non-committee members arrived on the day and held a meeting at the Yaowang Temple. At the same time, the first sub-bureau was notified by telephone to send a package of ginseng to the meeting for identification, but all the executive and supervisory committee members of the Pharmaceutical Association believed that the store had illegally convened the meeting and there was no need to attend, so they ignored it. Yesterday, the Pharmaceutical Association received another letter from a gentleman from the noodle industry, sending a package of ginseng, saying that it was also purchased from Li Tongfeng and was a fake product and an inferior product, requesting identification. According to people in the pharmaceutical industry, real American ginseng sold on the market costs 167 yuan per two, but the so-called real American ginseng sold by the store costs 4 yuan per two. Regardless of its authenticity, even according to the store clerk's own admission that it is a defective product, it is already a substandard medicine, similar to fraudulent behavior. In addition, there is also a kind of artificially cultivated Oriental ginseng that is very easy to distinguish, and it is known to be an inferior product at a glance. The pharmacies in this city never use it, because according to the pharmaceutical business regulations, the ginseng and medicine used are related to people's lives, and all must use top-grade genuine goods. Substandard second-grade goods are all subject to crackdown. As for the package of American ginseng sold by Li Tongfeng this time, the association is reluctant to be responsible for certification because it is a matter of friendship with the same industry. However, now that it has been transferred to the court for interrogation, it can only wait quietly for the court's judgment. If the court requests identification in the future, it can only handle it impartially and not want to be biased and deceive oneself and others.

Wu Shutang, a resident of Xintangli, the fifth district of the county, has some assets. Yesterday was the wedding of his son Xifang. The day before yesterday, he hosted a banquet for guests. Large Fire in West Street, Nantong City

West Street in Tongcheng is a bustling commercial area and the essence of the city. At about 2 a.m. on the 30th, a fire suddenly broke out in the Jingfuzhai Food Store, and in an instant, it spread to 17 stores, including Fuji Cloth Store, Yuyuan Clock Store, and Sino-British Pharmacy. The entire central section was turned to ashes. The fire was completely extinguished at noon, and the loss was in the range of 500,000 yuan, which is a catastrophic robbery unprecedented in this city. As for the cause of the fire, it was caused by a short circuit in the electric lights of the store. The stone archway in the central market of West Street was also burned down, and the stone pillars were broken.

Local News: Fujian-Zhejiang Border Has Not Been Engaged; Shanghai-Fujian Telegraph Line Remains Open

The New Voice News Agency reports: Recently, there have been widespread rumors in Shanghai that Fujian troops have clashed with Zhejiang forces near the Xianxia Ridge. However, the central army units under Liu Heding and Zhou Hunyuan are all stationed in northern Fujian. If the 19th Route Army intends to advance north, it would be difficult for them to reach the base of Xianxia Ridge directly. Furthermore, the Shanghai-Fuzhou telegraph line passes through Jiangshan in Zhejiang, across Xianxia Ridge, and south to Pucheng. If hostilities were to occur, the telegraph line would inevitably be cut. As the Shanghai-Fuzhou telegraph line remains open, it is evident that the rumors of engagement are entirely unfounded.

Visitor from Pingyang Discusses: Wenzhou and Ruian Areas are Peaceful; However, Shipments from Shanghai Have Sharply Decreased

Pingyang, in the Wenzhou prefecture of Zhejiang, borders Fujian province. Since the Fujian Incident, merchants from Pingyang have mostly stopped trading. Yesterday, the Xinruiping vessel of the Shanghai Huxing Company arrived in Shanghai from Pingyang. Our reporter made a special trip to the vessel to inquire about the situation. The obtained information is detailed below:

Peace in Pingyang

The Xinruiping vessel specializes in the Shanghai-Ruian-Pingyang route. It arrived in Shanghai at 3:00 PM yesterday, docking in the Nanshi district. The vessel was heavily loaded, mainly with coal. Many passengers also arrived in Shanghai. The head of the Pingyang Consolidated Tax Bureau traveled to Shanghai on this vessel. According to the crew, when the Xinruiping left Pingyang on the 29th, the area was peaceful and the people felt relatively secure. Pingyang is separated from the Fujian border by the Fen Shui Ling, a distance of several hundred li, mostly through mountainous terrain, making travel very difficult.

Reinforcements of Warships

A few days ago, due to troop deployments in Taishun County, which borders Zhejiang and Fujian, there were false rumors of a military mutiny, causing considerable anxiety among the people in the Ruiping area. The Zhejiang Overseas Water Police Bureau dispatched the warship Yongping to be stationed there. The Yongping is currently docked in Pingyang for the purpose of providing local defense.

Wenzhou is Safe

Currently, four vessels operate on the Shanghai-Wenzhou route. Recently, due to the large shipments of food supplies that have been completed, Wenzhou merchants are rushing to prepare for New Year's goods. Although merchants have not stopped trading due to the impact of the Fujian Incident, they have curtailed loans due to tight credit conditions. As a result, cargo shipments from Shanghai to Wenzhou have plummeted, reaching only half the usual volume. Yesterday, the Lian'an Shipping Bureau sent a telegram inquiring about the situation in the area. They received a reply in the afternoon stating that the situation in Wenzhou was stable, so the Shanghai-Wenzhou liners are all operating as usual.

Ample Fujian Goods

The navy has not yet blockaded the port of Sanduao. Yesterday, Jardine Matheson's vessel Jiesheng left for Fuzhou as usual at around 2:00 PM. Shanghai-based Fujian merchants shipped a total of 700 tons of goods, a twofold increase compared to the previous shipment, mainly textiles. Many passengers traveling to Fujian also departed on this vessel from Shanghai.

Beijing Denies Rumors of Chiang's Resignation

The New Voice News Agency reports that a certain foreign newspaper in Shanghai previously published news that Chairman Chiang was considering resigning. According to a central government official speaking to a reporter stationed in Beijing for the New Voice News Agency, the rumors of Chairman Chiang's resignation circulating in Shanghai on the (30th) are completely unfounded.

Shanghai's Various Sectors to Hold an Anti-Rebellion Rally Today; Wu Tiecheng and Eleven Others Elected to Presidium; Venue Ready at Public Stadium

The civic anti-rebellion rally initiated by various sectors of Shanghai is scheduled to take place at the Dalin Road Public Stadium at 2:00 PM today. The Municipal Public Security Bureau, fearing that reactionary elements may take the opportunity to engage in activities, has temporarily stepped up security measures. Details are as follows:

Venue Setup: The venue is the Municipal First Public Stadium on Dalin Road. The Kuomintang flag and national flag are hung at the main entrance, along with a white banner reading "Shanghai Civic Anti-Rebellion Rally". A temporary platform with a reed canopy is set up in the middle of the north side of the stadium. Observations on the Current Situation After the Fujian Incident: Reporter from Shenshi News Agency Flies from Fujian to Shanghai Yesterday; The Reported Situation

The Shenshi News Agency reports that since the coup in Fujian Province, rumors have been rampant. The Shenshi News Agency dispatched a reporter to fly to Guangdong and then to Fujian some days ago. He returned to Shanghai from Fuzhou yesterday afternoon. The various pieces of information he has obtained are detailed below:

Military Reorganization

According to the Shenshi News Agency reporter's extensive investigations in Fuzhou, the actual military strength of Chen Mingshu, Li Jishen, and others after the coup in Fujian consists of approximately 40,000 troops in the main force of the 19th Route Army, supplemented by miscellaneous troops, totaling no more than 60,000. The organization is as follows: 1st Army Commander Shen Guangdian, Deputy Commander Li Chengzong; 2nd Army Commander Mao Weishou, Deputy Commander Zhang Li; 3rd Army Commander Qu Shounian, Deputy Commander Huang Gu; 4th Army Commander Zhang Yan; 5th Army Commander Tan Qixiu; 1st Division Commander Liu Zhanxiong; 2nd Division Commander Pang Cheng; 3rd Division Commander Zhang Junsong; 4th Division Commander Situ Fei; 5th Division Commander Xie Shousheng; 7th Division Commander Zhao Yijian; 60th Division Commander Deng Zhicai; 61st Division Commander Liang Shiji; 71st Division Commander Ying Yunlin; 49th Division Commander Hong Huanbao. The numbers in each army are mostly insufficient and they are actively being replenished and trained. Recently, Weng Zhaoyuan has also been heavily involved in reorganizing the militia. It has now been decided that there will be five general brigades, divided into four detachments, led by Chen Weijin, Peng Tang, Zhang Xiongnan, and Lin Jing as detachment commanders, with a strength of approximately 3,000 men. In terms of air power, only twelve aircraft are available for combat.

Lifting of Martial Law in the Provincial Capital

After the establishment of the People's Government, martial law was imposed by the city defense commander due to the tense situation. It was lifted on the 27th of last month, and people can now move freely at night. However, people wishing to leave Fuzhou are still subject to strict restrictions and must report in detail to the Provincial Public Security Bureau and obtain permission before leaving the province. However, when the reporter left Fuzhou, large luggage was still strictly prohibited from leaving the city.

Resolutions Passed

The meeting then adjourned.

Cooperation Between State-Run and Private Shipping Industries in Water-Land Transportation: | This is the First Step Towards Recovering Shipping Rights | The Joint Office Will Be Established Upon Order; The Allocation Method Will Be Determined Based on Routes and Vessels

The New Voice News Agency reports that the state-run China Merchants Steam Navigation Company is handling national water-land transportation, and various private shipping companies are striving to join. After the Ministry of Railways decided on a cooperation method between state-run and private companies, companies such as Sanbei are organizing a joint office. Details are as follows:

Organization of Joint Office

The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company is handling national water-land transportation. In addition to the Longhai Railway, which was implemented on the 20th of last month, the Tianjin-Pukou, Beining, Pinghan, Jinghu, Huhu-Ningbo, Zhengda, Daoqing, Pingsui, Jiaoji, Xiang'e and ten other railways were originally scheduled to be implemented yesterday. Now, the implementation has been postponed due to the private sector's joining the intermodal transport case. After the state-run China Merchants Steam Navigation Company and the private Sanbei Company receive orders from the Ministry of Railways, they will convene a meeting of various private shipping companies to organize a joint office for private and state-run shipping industries, implement cooperation, and then separately handle national railway intermodal transport.

Prelude to Recapturing Shipping Rights

A reporter from the New Voice News Agency met with Yu Qiaqing, general manager of Sanbei Company, yesterday. According to him, the Ministry of Railways has decided on a cooperation method for the private shipping industry's participation in the intermodal transport case, which will be handled by a joint office organized by state-run and private companies. Preparations will begin in Shanghai as soon as the ministry's order arrives. In the future, the allocation of various railway intermodal transport services will be determined based on the routes and vessels operated by each shipping company, with a cooperative spirit and mutual adjustment. This method is actually the first step in fundamentally recovering shipping rights.

International Silk Conference Passes Resolution to Restrict Dumping of Japanese Silk

In recent years, the dumping of Japanese silk to foreign countries has attracted international attention. Therefore, at this International Silk Conference, a resolution was passed to restrict the import volume of Japanese silk. Our country's envoy to France, Gu Weijun, has telegraphed the Ministry of Foreign Affairs with the details of the conference's resolution, which has been forwarded to the Ministry of Industry and Commerce for information. The International Trade Bureau of this city received the Ministry's instruction yesterday. The instruction stated that Envoy Gu in Paris telegraphed that at the International Silk Conference, an agreement was reached, based on the proposal of the British delegation, to oppose the dumping of all kinds of Japanese silk products, and each representative would negotiate with their respective governments to restrict the amount of Japanese silk imports to a maximum of the average amount between 1927 and 1930. The American and Italian representatives felt that this method was too harsh and suggested changing it to a proposal to the Japanese silk industry, but it was not passed. In addition to instructing the consulate general to report in detail, please forward it to the Ministry of Industry and Commerce. The Ministry, in addition to issuing orders and awaiting a detailed report from the consulate general before issuing further orders, hereby orders the bureau to inform and forward it to silk industry organizations for their information.

Aftermath of the Taikoo Strike Remains Unsettled; Business Community Dissatisfied with Lack of Compensation for Inventory Losses; Workers Question Restructuring, Telegraph Guangdong to Inquire About Terms

According to Xin Sheng News Agency, since the resolution of the labor-management dispute at the Taikoo Company in Guangzhou on the 15th of last month, the employees of the Foshan freighter resumed work on the 27th. The business community in Guangdong expressed dissatisfaction that the company did not provide compensation for significant losses and telegraphed various locations to refuse to load Taikoo vessels. The workers of the Wusong freighter held a meeting yesterday to discuss resuming work and decided to continue discussions today. The details are as follows:

Route Resumption

Over one hundred employees of the Taikoo Hong Kong-Guangzhou freighter Foshan, who had been on strike for seven months due to dissatisfaction with the company's handling of the Wusong freighter workers, resumed work in Guangzhou at noon on the 27th of last month after the labor-management negotiations in Guangzhou resulted in the company compensating the actors for losses of 160,000 Guangdong silver dollars. Dock workers and Taikoo warehouse workers also simultaneously resumed work. The Taikoo Nanhua freighter also resumed the Guangzhou route at the same time.

Business and Industry Dissatisfied

Various business groups such as the Guangzhou-Hong Kong Grain Association,封鎖 Taikoo warehouses to facilitate negotiations for the Guangdong sailors, causing Taikoo inventories to suffer mildew and losses exceeding five million yuan. At the time, it was hoped that compensation would be obtained after the negotiations were resolved. Also, the workers in the civilian boat hostels and other industries opposed it because they refused to sell Taikoo tickets and unload goods at the time, and now there is no compensation. Therefore, they rose up in opposition, issued a declaration, and telegraphed to refuse to load Taikoo vessels.

Restructuring of Vessels

The resolution of the Wusong freighter case in Guangzhou included six terms, including the complete resumption of work by the Wusong freighter workers. Within one month, the company will carry out a reorganization. In addition to those working on the ships, each person will be given 25 yuan for dismissal. The company will notify the resumption period in advance, register and pay wages. Gao Kunquan, a worker who was kidnapped and disappeared, will be handed over by the company within two weeks. There is also an attached clause stipulating that the company will continue to restructure the vessels.

Workers Gather to Discuss

The 126 workers in the Wusong freighter's middle cabin have been unemployed for a year, experiencing great hardship. Now that work is resuming, there will still be reductions, and they suspect that it is called restructuring. They held a meeting at the Middle Cabin Company on Jiuxiaochang Road at 2:00 PM yesterday and decided: (1) Telegraph the Guangdong Seamen's Union to inquire about the terms of the resolution. (2) Continue discussing the resumption of work at 2:00 PM tomorrow (today).

Ning Shao Company Marine Engineer Salary Increase Dispute Resolved; Social Affairs Bureau Convened Mediation Yesterday; Both Parties Signed Three Measures

According to the Dagong News Agency, marine engineers of the Ning Shao Company's Ning Shao, Ning Jing, and Xin Ning Shao freighters have traditionally received double pay at the end of the year. However, other shipping companies do not have this double pay system. Therefore, the company was questioned by its competitors and announced in July of this year that it would abolish the double pay and instead increase the monthly salary. However, the agreed-upon measures were considered uneven by both parties, leading to a dispute and a request to the Social Affairs Bureau for mediation. After receiving the request, the bureau feared that a dispute would arise, affecting transportation. It immediately sent personnel to investigate the truth and persuaded both parties to negotiate a settlement. After more than a month, there was still no news from either party. In order to seek a swift resolution, the bureau convened mediation yesterday. Feng Yuming from the labor side and Lu Ziyang and Chen Renzheng from the capital side, and Chen Shiqi from the Party Department attended. Zhu Jintao from the Social Affairs Bureau presided, and Wang Zhiqin recorded. After repeated negotiations between the two parties, a satisfactory solution was reached. From November onwards, the salary scales of the marine engineers of each freighter were set, and the capital side also expressed its recognition. The settlement measures were then signed as follows: (1) The salary scales of the marine engineers of the Xin Ning Shao, Ning Jing, and Ning Shao freighters of the Ning Shao Shipping Company have been revised due to the cancellation of the year-end double pay, as follows: (A) Xin Ning Shao: Chief Engineer, 250 yuan per month; First Engineer, 165 yuan; Second Engineer, 100 yuan; Coppersmith, 55 yuan. (B) Ning Jing: Chief Engineer, 200 yuan per month; First Engineer, 160 yuan; Second Engineer, 100 yuan. (C) Ning Shao: Chief Engineer, 190 yuan per month; First Engineer, 145 yuan; Second Engineer, 100 yuan.

Shanghai-Ningbo-Suzhou Tobacco and Alcohol Industries Petition the Ministry of Finance to Revise Tax Regulations

The Shanghai-Ningbo-Suzhou Tobacco Industry Association Union and the Alcohol Industry Association Union have repeatedly protested regarding the new tax regulations, but to no avail. As a result, merchants and related workers in both industries feel exceptionally distressed. They have elected Yu Xunlu, Zhang Suhou, Zhang Dalian, Chen Weiwen, and others as eight petition representatives to go to Beijing on the 25th, convene the representatives, and discuss two concrete measures: (1) Petition for revision of the tax regulations. (2) Accuse Xie Qi, the Director of the Tax Affairs Department. On the 30th, they went to the Executive Yuan, the Control Yuan, and the Ministry of Finance to petition and submit a memorial. The original text of their memorial to the Executive Yuan and the Control Yuan was published in yesterday's newspaper. Now, we have obtained the original text of their memorial to the Ministry of Finance and transcribe it below:

Presenting a memorial regarding the new tobacco and alcohol system, whose provisions are harsh and cumbersome, restricting business and causing distress to taxpayers. We respectfully dispatch representatives to petition, hoping that you will examine and grant a proper revision, so as to increase tax revenue and alleviate the difficulties of businesses. It is our humble opinion that since the beginning of this year, the Tax Affairs Department has abolished the old tobacco and alcohol monopoly system and revised the special tax on native tobacco leaves and the fixed tax on native alcohol. The rules and regulations promulgated are meticulous and restrictive, no less than placing tobacco and alcohol merchants in a dead end. Our Association has repeatedly drafted summaries and petitioned for revisions, but has not been approved. Merchants paying taxes is an obligation to be fulfilled, and showing compassion for the people is an essential part of governance. Now, the government, facing an empty treasury, seeks ways to increase revenue, and merchants share the difficulties, responding to all requests. However, the tax authorities do not understand, demanding without end. They either find fault with incomplete procedures or impose severe penalties for non-compliance with the regulations. This new system has been in effect for five months, and the failure to reconcile with business conditions is the source of frequent disputes. We hereby present a brief account, item by item, for your Lordship's review and grant of revisions, so that both tax authorities and merchants can benefit. (1) Unequal Tax Rates: In the case of imitation Shaoxing wine (i.e., Suzhou-made native yellow wine by Shaoxing merchants), if it is native yellow wine, the tax rate is 80 cents per 100 jin. However, for the Suzhou-made native yellow wine by Shaoxing merchants, the tax authorities cleverly create a name, imitation Shaoxing wine, and the tax rate is 1 yuan and 40 cents per 100 jin, an increase of 60 cents. For Shaoxing wine merchants from various counties in Zhejiang Province who produce yellow wine, the same tax is levied as native yellow wine, without distinguishing the merchants' origin. Furthermore, for Shaoxing wine produced in Shaoxing, the tax rate is 1 yuan and 40 cents, and in the sales area, it is 2 yuan. Production and sales in Zou Province should be average, so how can there be a sudden increase of 60 cents? Moreover, Shaoxing merchants also produce yellow wine, which has always been taxed at the same rate as native yellow wine, without distinguishing the origin of the wine merchants (because the raw materials of Shaoxing yellow wine are not different from those of local yellow wine, and the selling price is about the same). It should be treated equally as Suzhou products. As for Shaoxing wine, because it is produced in the old Shaoxing Prefecture and sold outside the area, the customary name is Shaoxing wine. Those sold within the old Shaoxing Prefecture are still called yellow wine. The tax authorities have set different tax rates for yellow wine produced in the old Shaoxing Prefecture of Zhejiang Province. Shaoxing wine is 1 yuan and 40 cents per 100 jin, while yellow wine produced in other counties is taxed as native yellow wine at 1 yuan per 100 jin. Furthermore, the provincial tax on Shaoxing wine produced within the production area is 86 cents and 4 li per 100 jin, and the monopoly fee is 80 cents, totaling 1 yuan 66 cents and 4 li. When the Suzhou tax system was reformed, the provincial tax was abolished long ago, and only the monopoly fee was levied at 1 yuan and 20 cents per 100 jin. Merchants raised funds, and the actual payment was 76 cents and 8 li per 100 jin. Now, the new tax system is based on the original 20% of the monopoly fee, so why does Shaoxing wine alone increase by 1 yuan? The actual tax rate is increased by 1 yuan 23 cents and 2 li per 100 jin, making it clear that the sales area is more heavily taxed than the production area. Also, in the past, native yellow wine from the upper districts had no tax in the concessions and half tax (i.e., special levy) in the Chinese areas. Now, under the new system, taxation cannot be effectively implemented in the concessions, and the half tax is immediately abolished in the Chinese areas, forcing the collection of the full tax. The above is clear evidence of unequal tax rates. (2) Extortion Along the Way: In the past, during the chaotic war era, merchants transporting goods only needed to pay the required tax to pass unhindered. Now, under the new tax system, even after paying taxes and obtaining a license, the goods are inspected along the way, examining their credentials, in a manner similar to variable Likin taxes. Furthermore, there are deliberate delays and difficulties, requiring payments to pass. For example, 69 pieces of tobacco collected in Jiangyin were extorted 10 cents per piece during inspection in Suzhou-Wuxi, totaling 6 yuan and 90 cents. Also, 15 pieces of Zhuoyun tobacco leaves were extorted 1 yuan per piece by the Guandong-Ganzhou branch, totaling 15 yuan (both of the above cases have been investigated and filed by the association with the Jiangsu Tobacco and Alcohol Tax Bureau). Also, the four boats of Taiyu Zhang's liquor passed through Hengtang Town in Suzhou-Wuxi, and the liquor tax had been paid in accordance with regulations and certificates affixed. However, a patrolling officer Xu falsely claimed that the tax stickers were insufficient, forcibly demanding a huge tax of 200 dan and threatening to impose a fine of 5,000 yuan. In fact, they wanted to extort money for the pass. Later, the merchant reported to the relevant department and asked them to verify the tax amount, which was consistent. In theory, the case should have been dismissed. However, the inspector, failing to extort money, falsely accused the special investigator of assault and sent the merchant to the local public security bureau, detaining him for five days. The above three examples are clear evidence of extortion along the way. (3) Severe Penalties: In the past, Shaoxing wine from Taixing shipped to Shanghai was calculated at five or eight parts. This time, the revised new system specifies that it should be calculated at seven or five parts. Taxes were supplemented in accordance with regulations, but the inspectors still re-examined them and determined that they did not match, forcing the calculation at eight parts. The remaining 40 dan or so were considered to be merchants deliberately trying to take advantage and evade taxes. The affixed tax certificates were completely invalidated, and taxes were re-collected. Furthermore, the liquor skins were confiscated, and a similar amount of fines was levied. This is clear evidence of severe penalties. (4)

Page 14

Resembles Double Taxation: The government has clearly ordered that one item be taxed only once. The existing tobacco and alcohol inventories have already paid the monopoly tax and fee. Of course, if the goods have already been taxed, then even if the new system is revised, there is no reason for double taxation. Otherwise, it is clear evidence of resembling double taxation. (5) Disparate Treatment: The fixed tax on native alcohol is divided into categories, and the tax rates are set accordingly. However, the special tax on native tobacco leaves does not distinguish between high and low grades, and the same 4 yuan 15 cents is levied per 100 jin. For high-grade tobacco leaves worth 70 or 80 yuan, 4 yuan 15 cents are levied, while for low-grade leaf and autumn leaves worth 13 yuan, the same 4 yuan 15 cents is levied. The cost difference is enormous. The tax rates should be set according to the quality of the alcohol. Otherwise, it is clear evidence of disparate treatment. The Association has the state's tax revenue at heart and considers the difficulties of merchants. It has no choice but to appeal for relief. It has specially appointed Yu Xunlu, Zhang Dalian, Cao Gexian, Gao Youming, Jin Jingjie, Zhang Suhou, Ru Baiquan, and Wang Xingguo to be petition representatives and seek redress, presenting their grievances in person. It is appropriate to submit a memorial, hoping that your Lordship will examine and adopt it, quickly revise and improve the new system's regulations, so that tax revenue will be prosperous and merchants will have convenience, in line with the purpose of enriching taxes and pacifying merchants. With utmost respect, we respectfully submit this to Minister Kong of the Ministry of Finance of the National Government.

Ministry of Railways Stipulates Regulations for Luggage Crossing the River Fee: Free Weight Should Be Deducted First

The Two Railways Administration received Instruction No. 7433 from the Ministry of Railways yesterday, which read: "Regarding the report from the Hunan-Hubei Section Administration of the Yuehan Railway, stating, 'Whether the luggage crossing the river fee should be calculated based on weight, or whether the free weight should be deducted, please check and instruct, etc.' Based on this, it is found that the regulations for the railway transportation of luggage have provisions for free limits for each class. The ferry crossing fee should be handled uniformly, first deducting the free weight stipulated in the Passenger Car Transportation Rules, and then calculating the crossing fee. In addition to Xu's instructions and sub-instructions, you should be aware of this order." The Administration has forwarded this order to the Transportation Department for compliance.

It can reduce gasoline consumption. On the 2nd, 9th, and 14th of this month, we gathered fourteen companies from the industry at appropriate locations and conducted three on-site tests using various methods. Sudden Death Dispute of Noodles Shop Apprentice: Awaiting Forensic Examination

Zhong Baogen, who runs a noodle shop in Tangjiawan outside Ximen, is from Danyang. Wang Xiaohai, an eighteen-year-old fellow townsman of the woman Wang Zhao, was an apprentice in his shop. He suddenly died in September. Zhong immediately arranged for a hasty encoffining and ordered someone to send the body back to Danyang for burial. Wang Zhao had not yet learned of this. She came to Shanghai to look for her son. Zhong claimed that he died from heatstroke, but the body was not shown. The woman inquired with the neighbors, who all said that Wang Xiaohai was first severely beaten by Zhong for embezzling a dime of auxiliary currency. In the evening, he was tied to the flour-grinding machine and electrocuted to death. Because the foolish deed was discovered, he was immediately buried, and so on. The woman, believing that her son died an unnatural death and that the body was destroyed, filed a complaint with the local court. Zhong Baogen was arrested. He still claimed that the death was due to an epidemic, and that the coffin was sent back to the mother, but she had not received it. Since the testimonies in this case are contradictory, the matter cannot be clarified without turning over the coffin for examination. Therefore, Zhong was released on bail. Zhong has now transported the coffin from Danyang by private boat to the river under Xinzha Bridge. He reported this to the court yesterday. The Chief Prosecutor, Lou Ying, officially instructed the police to have the plaintiff and defendant send the coffin to the Zhenru Forensic Examination Office for an initial opening. After both parties identify the body, a surgical autopsy will be performed to determine the cause of death and to investigate the internal organs to determine how he died, pending further investigation.

Kuang Hu Drowns Herself in River for Seven Yuan Debt: Rescued and Spared from Drowning

Kuang Hu, an elderly woman from Suzhou, residing at No. 142 Guangqi Road inside Xiaodongmen, is fifty-eight years old. Her husband has been dead for many years, and her family is impoverished. Her only son is also indolent, spending all day outside and not pursuing a proper career, leaving the woman without any support. She relies solely on her ten fingers to make lace for others. This summer, due to a pressing need, she borrowed seven yuan from her relative, Zhou Hu. Aside from two yuan already repaid, she still owed five yuan. The other day, Zhou Hu went to Kuang Hu's residence to demand the loan. Because she had no money to pay, she was scolded by Zhou Hu, causing her extreme anger. Thinking that her late years were meaningless, she had the thought of committing suicide. She went out alone and walked to the Bund outside Sima Road. Taking advantage of people's inattention, she sighed and jumped into the river, hoping to end her life and finish her remaining years. Fortunately, a passerby saw her and quickly called on boatmen to rescue her from the water, allowing her to be reborn. The police were immediately notified and brought her to the police station. After questioning by the chief, since she lived in the Chinese concession, around 9 PM the previous evening, officer Yang Zaishan was dispatched to send her to the No. 2 section of the No. 1 district of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, and she was transferred to the Municipal Public Security Bureau around 1 PM yesterday for arrangements.

Fourth District Public Security Bureau Cracks Down on Male and Female Child Traffickers

Recently, child trafficking has been rampant in the Zhabei area, and advertisements seeking lost children have been posted everywhere. It has come to light that Xu Zhihui (32 years old, from Yangzhou), who runs a grocery store named "Xu Xia Tai" at No. 216, the intersection of Gonghe Xin Road and Jiaotong Road, had a three-year-old daughter named Rongmei who was abducted by bandits around 1 PM on November 21. Xu immediately sent out detectives in all directions, but could not find her. Until the other day, someone reported that Rongmei had been trafficked to a thatched shed under the No. 1 bridge of Ximei Road in the Fen District of the Fifth District Public Security Bureau, behind the Fenshui Temple, and so on. That evening, Xu hired a car to go to the station, and reported to the Xinkang Police Station, who dispatched police to arrest them in the thatched shed. However, the child traffickers had already escaped, having heard the news. Later, Xu discovered that Rongmei was hidden on a small boat in that location, so he went to check the boat again. Indeed, he saw Rongmei and two other children sleeping on the boat. At that time, the male and female accomplices of the child traffickers, Wang Si and his wife, Tian, were arrested. Because the case originated in the Fourth District of Zhabei and involved the capture of the remaining accomplices, Xu immediately took Wang Si and his wife, as well as Rongmei, in a car to Zhabei. According to Wang Si's confession, he is 31 years old and from Funing. Wang Tian claimed to be 30 years old. Both stated that Rongmei was entrusted to them for foster care by their friend Wang Liu, who lived at No. 40, Liuhe Lane, Jiangmiao Road, at the end of Datong Road. The Fourth District Public Security Bureau ordered Police Chief Chen Maoxiu of the Zhongxing Road Precinct to lead the police to Liuhe Lane and arrest Wang Liu. However, Liu's name Xin Di had already fled. After bringing the case to trial, Wang Liu, 29 years old and from Taizhou, confessed. She remained silent about the abduction of Rongmei. After examining the confession, the interrogating officer ruled that the case involved the abduction of a child and ordered that it be sent to the Public Security Bureau for disposal. It is also rumored that the child traffickers had just come to Shanghai from Wuxi, and had many accomplices. They entrusted the Shanghai-based bandits to lure and abduct children everywhere, and then transport them to Shantou and Xiamen to sell them for profit.
