Shanghai National Crisis Propaganda Troupe's Mongolian Border and Northwest Exhibition Opens: Held for Ten Days at the Civic Education Center Starting Yesterday: Second Long-Distance Propaganda Tour Begins After Closing: Chairman Lin and Others Inscribe Gifts

The Mongolian Border and Northwest Exhibition has been actively preparing. Because new, large paintings needed to be added, it was delayed until yesterday morning before it officially opened. The organizers of the exhibition are Shen Qianyi, head of the Shanghai National Crisis Propaganda Troupe, and seven members of his troupe. They have been setting up at the Civic Education Center for days and were ready yesterday. Visitors came in an endless stream. The details are as follows.

Open-Air Exhibition

Upon entering, there is a large horizontal cloth banner with the words "Shanghai National Crisis Propaganda Troupe's Mongolian Border and Northwest Exhibition." The most eye-catching feature of the exhibition is the large oil paintings hanging on the walls of the Confucius Temple Park. The large ones are several zhang long, and the small ones are also square zhang or seven or eight chi. They all depict the scenery of the Mongolian border and the Great Wall, the tragic scenes of Japanese massacres, or allegorical paintings to awaken the people. There are dozens of them, covering almost all the walls outside the Dacheng Gate, Dacheng Hall, Minglun Hall, and Chongsheng Ancestral Hall, shocking viewers.

Sketches from Various Places

The first and second exhibition halls are in the Health Exhibition Room of the Civic Education Center. The sketches and photographs on display are signed with place names, such as Guihua, Suiyuan, Yingfang, Weinan, Baotou Yinshan, Longmen, Yaoxian, Jin Suo Guan, Xuanhua, Zhangjiakou, Fushi County, Jing Shuidu, Xuanyuan Tomb, Zhaojun Tomb, Northern Shaanxi, Yijun, Datong, etc. The paintings all come from sketches from the actual sites, which can give a glimpse of the customs and humanity of the border areas.

Northwest Products

The third exhibition hall, in the music room of the center, has even more displays. In addition to paintings and sketches, there are various products from the Mongolian border and the Northwest, such as Baotou's woolen yarn, wool grabs, etc. There are also artistic carpets, all woven by Mongolian natives. The troupe members drew the designs, so they are very beautiful. According to the troupe leader, Mr. Shen, if this kind of product can be improved, it can exceed imported goods by a hundred times. Its solid quality can guarantee use for a hundred years. There are countless amounts of sheep wool and real camel wool abandoned on the ground outside the pass, which is a pity. In addition, there are many varieties of Western Xia script, Mongolian script, Tibetan script, and Manchu script on display.

Inscriptions from Important People

Lin Sen, chairman of the National Government, inscribed to the troupe, saying, "Expressing the enthusiasm for saving the country and relieving the people from suffering, developing it into art, this kind of work is of value." Zeng Zhongming, Vice Minister of the Ministry of Railways, inscribed the four characters "Art Saves the Country." Shao Lizi, Chairman of Shaanxi Province, inscribed the four characters "Awaken the People." The Mayor of this city inscribed the four characters "Shocking to the Eye." In addition, there are many inscriptions from important people, hanging on the four walls in a dazzling array.

Exhibition for Ten Days

According to the troupe leader, the exhibition will last for a total of ten days. After ten days, the troupe will have a second trip to the Northwest, going to Qinghai, Xinjiang, and Tibet, and then circling to the Southwest for a grand tour of thousands of miles. The Central Government has also entrusted them with a certain investigation mission. As for those who supported the troupe this time, on the Shanghai side there are Wang Xiaolai, Yu Qiaqing, Lin Kanghou, Du Yuesheng, Yu Hongjun, Huang Yanpei, Wu Kaixian, Wang Yansong, Zhang Zilian, etc. This exhibition is also the urging of Mr. Lin Kanghou and Mr. Zhang Zilian as a farewell souvenir for the second distant tour.

Fraudulent Methods Become Increasingly Strange: Lead Ingots Turn into Silver: Three People Swindled One After Another: Two Swindlers Each Detained for Five Months

Zhao Niu, a Suzhou native residing at No. 475 Pushi Road in the French Concession, and Qian Huilin, a Songjiang native living next door at No. 27, Lane 475, are both wandering vagrants who specialize in fraud. Their tricks are not leftovers, but are often invented. In the past half year, the most common technique they have used is the technique of melting lead ingots into silver to swindle money from the general populace. Such as Ding Jinkang, who lives in the Southern Yao area of Hedde Road, Hou Rongsheng, the son of Hou Yuxiang, a resident of Panjiazhai in Xujiahui, and Zhu Zhijing, who lives at No. 67, Lane 546, Tiantong Road, have all lost money after being deceived by their words. Among them,

The Hou Family (Father and Son)

lost the most, reaching 325 yuan. Zhu lost 45 yuan, and Ding only 30 yuan. When these people used their tricks on Ding, they first showed him a lead ingot that looked like a Ding Sheng cake, claiming that it was raw silver, just excavated from Dongting Mountain. There were many such silver blocks in the mountain. If they were excavated, they would be easy to pick up. However, they needed labor costs, so they were unable to mine it. If they got funds, they would determine the time of excavation and the quantity of output based on the amount of funding. In order to strengthen Ding's confidence, they took a stove and lit a fire, crushed a corner of the so-called raw silver lead ingot, stored it in a container, and placed it on the stove fire to melt it. Later, they took it to a silver shop to estimate its composition. According to them,

It Was Indeed Pure Silver

Ding's suspicion vanished and his desire for profit suddenly moved him to promise to pay for the cost of mining. He collected 30 yuan and gave it all to them. These people then pretended to show their trust by giving Ding three lead ingots as collateral. They were extremely cunning. Once the lead ingot was smelted, it turned into pure silver. There was no mysterious effect in this, but rather the agility of the hand. They had pre-prepared several small pieces of raw silver in the bag in their sleeves. When the lead ingot was crushed and thrown into the container, they slightly displayed a trick to make the deceived person pay less attention. Then they exchanged the silver block for the lead block to complete the work. By the time Ding realized afterward that what he had received was lead and not silver, the swindlers had already

Vanished Without a Trace

Aside from reporting to the police station, there was no way to recover the loss. He could only sigh in vain. The circumstances of the Hou family being swindled were the same as Ding's. However, Zhu Zhijing seemed to be willingly caught in the snare. Zhu had spare rooms for rent. The swindler happened to pass by his door, so he went inside to look at the house. Zhu saw that he was holding a lead ingot, so he asked about it. The swindler realized that this person had already fallen into his trap, so he said the same things to him as he had said to Ding, and said that he had come to rent the house as a silver smelting site, and fabricated all sorts of lies about how superior the benefits were. Zhu indeed

Was Greatly Deceived

He gave them 45 yuan. A few days ago, Inspector Cai Liu and Detective Liu Chunshu of the Gordon Road Police Station first arrested Zhao Niu on Xinzha Road, and then went to Qian's house to arrest Qian Huilin. Qian Huilin, along with the lead ingots turned in by Ding Jinkang, were sent to the First Special District Local Court yesterday. Judge Huang Risheng brought them to trial. Qian Xunjiu, the police lawyer, stated that the two defendants had used fraudulent means to swindle money from Ding and others, and that the facts were confirmed by witnesses, and requested that they be punished according to law. Subsequently, Ding, Hou, and Zhu, the three swindled people, filed a case to prove the circumstances at the time. Questioning Zhao and Qian, the two criminals remained silent. Judge Huang immediately announced the verdict, sentencing each to five months of imprisonment as a warning, and confiscating the lead ingots.

Abandoned After Initial Infatuation: Ding Handu Accused: Cohabitation Agreement, Oaths of Eternal Love: Discarded After Time, Like an Autumn Fan: The Sad Story of Ms. He Ruidi

Ding Handu, the young owner of a money shop, is currently 28 years old and works at McGao Foreign Company at No. 29 Sichuan Road. In the spring of last year, he met He Ruidi, a woman from Ningbo. At that time, the woman was only 21 years old, with a graceful figure and beautiful appearance. He fell in love at first sight and became close friends. After a considerable period of time, their love also reached a boiling point. Because Ms. He did not have a fixed residence, Ding made a further move, requesting to cohabitate. Ms. He also agreed, and they built a golden house at No. 5, Baoanfang, behind the Slaughterhouse Company in the French Concession, as a

place to hide his beauty

Oaths of eternal love, feelings were harmonious. At that time, in order to win He's trust, Ding wrote a document, stating that if he abandoned her midway, Ding would be willing to compensate her with one thousand yuan for living expenses, to be received and held by He. After obtaining the document, He was secretly delighted, thinking that she would have lifelong support and no worries for the future. Therefore, she lived with Ding at ease. Later, because the address was small, they moved to No. 26, Daodeli, Beile Road. At that time, Ding's father controlled all his property rights, so he was quite short of money.

Had Considerable Savings

Therefore, all expenses and household expenses were borne by He. Unexpectedly, the beautiful scenery did not last long, and a storm suddenly arose in the river of love, and the feelings of the past were all gone, until they each refused to give way, and went to court. Ding Handu's father suddenly died, and all the inheritance was inherited by Ding. Once he had great power and was able to make ends meet, and also knowing that He Ruidi's savings had been almost exhausted over the years, the love had waned, and he suddenly changed his usual state, constantly

indulging in prostitution

His footprints became sparse, and he even disappeared completely. He, because all her clothes had been pawned and there was no way to borrow money, had to look for him everywhere, running around all day long, hoping to meet Ding again, or to regain his heart and renew their old relationship. On October 17, He's mother found out that Ding was entertaining in Room 119 of the Jielu Hotel on Xizang Road, and rushed to look for him. She indeed found him there, so she questioned him and asked for household living expenses. Unexpectedly, Ding not only refused, but also

Beating He's Mother

Causing a head injury and fainting to the ground. Ding took the opportunity to escape. When He woke up and saw that the building was empty, she could not help but feel great grief. Ding had a tiger and wolf heart (having defiled her body, defrauded her of her wealth, and finally abandoned her without care, not only not allowed by law, but also not allowed by morality). In a fit of anger, she hired lawyer Li Mo to accuse Ding Handu of abandonment under Article 309 of the Criminal Code in the First Special District Court, requesting that the defendant be summoned to court and

Punished According to Law

and to file a civil suit, ordering him to compensate the plaintiff for the savings, clothes, and other expenses used up, as well as the 20,000 yuan specified in the contract. The court accepted the complaint and ordered that the defendant be summoned and scheduled for questioning in the Fifth Criminal Court by Judge Huang Risheng yesterday afternoon. The defendant did not arrive, but lawyers Yan Guoshi and Wang Weizhen arrived in court to defend him. After Judge Huang briefly questioned the plaintiff He Ruidi, he ordered that the case be rescheduled for further questioning on the afternoon of December 9.

Water Company Letter to Real Estate Association: Newly Set Fee Payment Method

Since the British Water Company changed to using water meters, water fees have doubled. Property owners are unable to bear the extra water fees, so they refuse to pay, causing disputes. The Real Estate Association negotiated with the Water Company and issued a water usage record form for property owners to fill out and send to the association to clarify the actual situation. Recently, property owners have been sending in the completed record forms to the association, so that they can be submitted to the upcoming Water Fee Arbitration Committee. Yesterday, the Water Company also sent a letter to the association, detailing various methods of collecting fees for water meter usage and the levels for paying deposit cabinet fees. The original letter is recorded below: "Dear Sirs, according to the current water fee collection method, the owner of each district's house may request the company to enter into contracts with the individual houses within the house and the residents thereof, but the house owner must bear the cost of all necessary replacements on the water pipes, and pay a cash deposit cabinet to the company, the amount of which must be sufficient to offset the total value of each water meter, then the company can handle it. This deposit cabinet fee will be refunded when the house is transferred to a new owner, or when the water meter is removed. Regarding the deposit cabinet fee part of the above method, a reduced collection standard can now be adopted, that is, each half-inch (1-2) water meter will be charged a deposit cabinet fee of 47 yuan, and each 3/8-inch (8-8) water meter will be charged a deposit cabinet fee of 33 yuan. The amount of 47 yuan, calculated at an annual interest rate of 6%, is 2 yuan and 8 jiao and 2 fen, that is, 2 jiao and 3 fen and 5 li per month. Therefore, the owner of the house, if there is a situation where the water usage in the house of the resident is excessive, it is permissible to consider the remedial measure of installing separate water meters. Because after installing separate water meters, the responsibility for water fees is no longer borne, the rent can be reduced, then under these circumstances, it should not be difficult to find a way to compensate for this low interest amount. As for why it is necessary to collect a deposit cabinet fee, the opinion of our company is that if a deposit cabinet fee is not collected, and all users are allowed to install water meters at the company's expense, then in order to compensate for this cost, the company will

have to specially increase the charging price for domestic water usage. Moreover, our company has now decided to adopt a trial method. The separate water meters are usually installed outdoors, but now we are trying to put the water meter in a small iron box and install it near the water faucet inside each house. The cost of this installation method on the water pipe is particularly low, but if this trial method is not proper in fact in the future, then the usual method will be used to modify the water pipe so that the water meter can be installed outside the house, and the owner needs to bear all the modification costs. Our company, according to the method of separate water meter installation mentioned in the first section of this letter, has existed since the implementation of the water meter system, but in fact, the number of owners who use this separate installation method is not the majority, so our company has not prepared many small water meters in stock, so if there are too many requests for separate water meter installation, it can only be processed gradually. This is specially reported."

Public Works Bureau Cracks Down on Privately Owned Rickshaws Soliciting Passengers: And Asks the Public for Assistance in Banning Them

In the Public Concession, there are now privately owned rickshaws soliciting passengers everywhere, commonly called "Wild Chicken" charter cars. These rickshaw pullers often forge the names of the owners and fraudulently obtain licenses for privately owned rickshaws. There are also genuine charter car pullers who solicit passengers without their owners' knowledge in order to earn "extra money." These vehicles not only constitute unfair competition with public rickshaws (yellow rickshaws), but also increase traffic obstacles. The Public Works Bureau will now crack down on them and hopes for the public's assistance. First, immediately refuse to ride in these charter cars when encountered, and report to the nearby police. Second, charter car owners should try to prevent their pullers from soliciting passengers privately and consider whether their wages are sufficient to avoid providing an excuse. As for the Public Works Bureau, in the future, it will strictly check the names and addresses of the owners when applying for charter car licenses. If falsification is discovered, the license will be revoked immediately. It is hoped that the public will provide assistance at any time, which will not only benefit social order, but also provide a small supplement to the livelihood of yellow rickshaw pullers.

Report on the French Municipal Council Health Department's Examination of Huangpu River Water

The French Concession Municipal Council Health Department reported the examination of bacteria in the Huangpu River water and tap water in November 1933 of the Western calendar. The results of the examination are extracted and recorded as follows: (1) Huangpu River water: 58,000 bacteria per cubic centimeter, 360,000 clusters of E. coli per liter. (2) French Concession tap water: 12 bacteria per cubic centimeter, 0 clusters of E. coli per liter. Purification percentage 99.99%.

Industrial Accident Statistics: Public Concession November Report

According to reports from the Public Works Bureau Police Department and the Emergency Ambulance, industrial and occupational accidents in the Public Concession in November resulted in 7 deaths and 32 injuries. Among the injured, 22 were men and 10 were women. Among the dead, two were electrocuted, two were killed by the explosion and fire of dangerous goods, one fell from the elevator shaft because the elevator did not have an interlocking mechanism, so the iron door could be opened even when the elevator was not on that floor, and another fell from the scaffolding at the construction site. The other one was fatally injured by cargo dropped from a ship. In addition, eight of the injured were from textile factories, and three of them were injured because their loose clothing was dragged into the machine.

Public Utilities Bureau Agrees on Method for Taxicab Security Deposits; Trade Association Notifies All Car Companies After Receiving Approval Yesterday; Each Car Must Pay 200 Yuan in Full Before Being Licensed

Regarding the case of the taxicab trade association petitioning the Municipal Public Utilities Bureau to change the third-party insurance requirement for automobiles to a security deposit system, the Bureau, after joint discussion with the Public Safety and Social Affairs Bureaus, has granted approval and revised four items. Yesterday, upon receiving approval, the association immediately notified its members to comply. The method is recorded below as a notification: Regarding the matter of notification, the Shanghai Municipal Public Utilities Bureau's No. 925 decree states: "Received and noted. This case has been jointly discussed by representatives from the Public Safety Bureau, this Bureau, and the Social Affairs Bureau, and the following has been decided: (1) The original order requiring commercial vehicles to carry third-party insurance was established to protect victims' losses. The trade association's request to change to a security deposit system is consistent with the goal of compensating for losses of life and property of victims. The various difficulties in obtaining third-party insurance mentioned by the association are also not without reason and should be approved. (2) The original proposal to have each commercial vehicle pay a security deposit of only 20 yuan is too small. In the event of a major accident, it may not be sufficient to provide protection. The security deposit should be changed to 200 yuan per vehicle. However, given the varying economic conditions of each car company, it can be paid in five installments starting in 1933. (3) The above security deposit should be collected by the trade association and deposited into the Municipal Bank jointly with the competent authorities. In the future, if funds are needed to compensate for third-party losses, the association should submit a request to the competent bureau to jointly withdraw the funds from the Municipal Bank for payment. However, the association will be responsible for replenishing any withdrawn funds from the car company responsible for the accident within one month. (4) Starting in January 1934, when commercial vehicles in this city apply for license plates from the Public Utilities Bureau each quarter, they must present a certificate from the association proving that the car company has paid the first year's security deposit before a license plate will be issued. This procedure will be followed thereafter." In addition to reporting the above to the Municipal Government for record, this decree is hereby issued for the trade association to comply with, and the first year's security deposit must be collected and reported to this Bureau within ten days of receipt of this notice for joint deposit. Upon receipt of this, in addition to filing it for record, we hereby copy the original text and order all members to comply. This is specially notified. Shanghai Taxicab Trade Association.

Two Railway Offices Issue Notice on Measures to Prevent Cargo Damage and Loss

The Traffic Departments of the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railways have jointly issued a circular to all stations, stipulating measures to prevent cargo damage and loss: (A) Regarding less-than-carload (LCL) cargo along the way: (1) Employees at each station must strictly comply with the procedures stipulated in the various regulations and detailed rules of operation and must not be lenient or perfunctory. (2) Each traffic section chief and each freight inspector, etc., should at any time check whether the personnel of their respective stations are handling freight in accordance with the prescribed procedures. Any violations should be given a warning for the first offense and a demerit for the second offense. Anyone who receives three major demerits will be dismissed according to regulations. (3) (a) Regarding the Beijing-Shanghai line, from Shanghai to Beijing, it is divided into two sections: Shanghai-Changzhou (referred to as Section A) and Changzhou-Beijing (referred to as Section B). For cargo transported from each station in one section to stations within that section, the escort officer of that section is responsible for supervising the loading and unloading. (b) For cargo transported from each station in Section A (except Shanghai North Station) to stations in Section B, the escort officer of Section A is responsible for supervising the loading, and upon arrival at Changzhou Station, it is handed over to the escort officer of Section B, who is then responsible for supervising the unloading. (c) For cargo transported from each station in Section B (except Nanjing Station and Nanjing Riverside Station) to stations in Section A, the same handover applies. (d) For cargo transported from Shanghai North Station to stations in Section B, the escort officer of Section B is responsible for supervising the loading and unloading. (e) For cargo transported from Nanjing Station and Nanjing Riverside Station to stations in Section A, the escort officer of Section A is responsible for supervising the loading and unloading. (4) For cargo transported from Shanghai North, Nanjing, and Nanjing Riverside stations, it should be loaded into separate cars according to the section of the destination station (Section A or Section B) to avoid confusion. As for cargo transported from other stations in Section A or Section B, regardless of which section the destination station belongs to, it should be loaded into the car managed by the on-duty escort officer of the section where the originating station is located, to clarify responsibility. (5) Escort officers of Section A and Section B should be on duty and off duty at the same time and do not change shifts at Changzhou Station. When the train is traveling in Section A, the escort officer of Section B can sleep and rest, and vice versa when in Section B, the escort officer of Section A can sleep and rest. However, both Section A and Section B escort officers must wait until the train reaches the terminal station and the handover is clear before going off duty. (B) Regarding carload, carload of LCL, and consolidated LCL cargo, except for items 1 and 2 being the same as above: (3) Each freight station inspector, each cargo investigator, and specially dispatched personnel from this office should supervise the unloading of cargo at each station at any time and submit a daily list of unloading conditions to the office for review. The above measures shall be implemented from December 1st of this year.

Shanghai Shipping Bureau Requests the "Chao Wu" Warship to Move Berth Because it Obstructs the Waterway

The "Chao Wu" warship, belonging to the Zhejiang Offshore Water Police Department and under the jurisdiction of the Ningbo Defense Command, patrols the eastern Zhejiang coast. Last winter, the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's "Xinfeng" steamer, replacing the "Xinjiangtian" on the Ningbo route, collided with the "Chao Wu" warship upon entering Zhenhai, resulting in damage to both sides and leading to a major dispute. The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company sent personnel to conduct an on-site investigation and consulted with the Offshore Department to reach a settlement. A year has passed, and it is said that it has not yet been concluded. Since the incident, the "Chao Wu" warship has also moved its berthing location.

Difficult Navigation for Ningbo Steamers

Recently, the owners of the Shanghai-Ningbo steamers "Xin Ningshao" and "Xin Jiangtian," etc., reported to the Shanghai Shipping Bureau that the "Chao Wu" warship has recently moved and docked in the port of Zhenhai, obstructing the waterway between Shanghai and Ningbo. With the slightest carelessness, a collision could occur. All shipowners have reported to the Shanghai Shipping Bureau, requesting the company to send a letter to negotiate and ask the warship to move away as soon as possible, otherwise the Ningbo steamers will not be able to enter the port of Zhenhai. Ning Shao China Merchants believes that this matter is of great importance to navigation safety and sent a formal letter yesterday to discuss it.

Please Move Berth Quickly

Ning Shao China Merchants, etc., jointly sent a letter yesterday to the Ningbo Defense Commander, stating that since the collision between the "Xinfeng" and "Chao Wu" warship, the "Chao Wu" has not been berthing in Zhenhai but moved to another location. The warship has recently moved back to the port of Zhenhai, obstructing the waterway. It is not only hindering navigation but also prone to accidents. It is requested that the warship be ordered to move away as soon as possible to facilitate navigation and avoid danger. If the warship continues to berth in the port, the Shanghai-Ningbo steamers will not call at the port of Zhenhai for safety reasons.

Submarine Cable Buried in Pudong

Prohibition of Ships Anchoring

Various shipping companies yesterday sent letters to various merchant ships, stating that they had received letters from the Public Security Bureau and the Public Utilities Bureau, which stated that the Pudong Water and Electricity Company had signed a contract with the Zhabei Water and Electricity Company in February of this year to supply water and electricity. It was agreed to first lay a submarine cable from the north of Wuquan Road and the east of Jungong Road in Zhabei to Puhama, about 1,113 meters south of Qiujiang Port, across the Huangpu River to the distribution station of the Pudong Gaohang District Taojiazhai Pu. Now that the cable has been shipped from England to Shanghai, construction will begin soon. Chinese signs stating "Submarine Cable Crossing, No Anchoring" have been placed on both sides of the cable-laying site. English signs stating "Cable Crossing" are also being installed. It is expected that they will be completed soon where the cable is buried. For fear that ships coming and going will arbitrarily anchor there, causing damage to the cable and hindering water and electricity traffic, all responsibility and compensation will be borne by the ship. Please inform accordingly. Separate letters have also been sent to foreign merchant shipping companies, asking them not to anchor at the cable burial site to respect electricity policy.

It was named the Sihe Company, and the red pill brands were Xianma and Jinlong. The Japanese man, Doki Abe, lived at No. 1123 Broadway Road. Police detectives went to his place and found 75 rubber bags, which were used to package Jinlong brand red pills. Xianma brand was packaged in paper. The loft of the house was used by Abe to store the manufactured red pills as a warehouse. The rubber bags have been sent to the Japanese consulate. The red pill materials seized at Li Maosong's house have been sent to the Chemistry Department of the Public Works Department for examination. The defendants Wu Qingsheng and the other ten fully admitted last time that they were working in the red pill group. Wang Chengen was introduced to Li Maosong by Yang Changsheng and worked in the company making red pills, with a monthly salary of 30 yuan. The other defendants received only ten yuan or so. Yang Changsheng had previously seen newspaper reports about the No. 9 Nanzun Road operation being raided by the police. Because he was close to Tan Chutang, he lived at Li Maosong's place and, upon learning of it, rushed to Tan's place to report the arrest. The stock list seized at Li's place was presented for inspection. When Wu Qingsheng and the other ten were questioned, their statements were similar to their previous admissions. Wang Chengen testified that he was introduced to Li Maosong by Yang Changsheng and a Mr. Chen and worked at the operation, earning 30 yuan a month. He could make about 10,000 large or small red pills every night, about 15 or 16 bags. The boss, Li Maosong, would sometimes come to the company to supervise the production. Tan Chutang was also a shareholder. Yang Changsheng testified that he rented a pavilion room at Li Maosong's place, paying 10 yuan in rent. In the past, he had seen Japanese people come but did not bring red pills. He gave evasive answers to other questions. Judge Liu Yugui ordered that they be remanded in custody and scheduled a pronouncement of judgment.

Tragedy of a Vegetable Boat Sinking in the Wind; Boat Owner Shi Hongchun Drowned on the Spot

The Jiangbei sand boat Shi Changtai, Shanghai Customs imprint No. 560, loaded with 6,000 heads of Chinese cabbage from Taiping Port in Jiangbei to Shanghai for sale. At 6:00 PM the other day, it arrived at the Sanjiashui Estuary in Wusong. At that time, it encountered a sudden storm. The boat's helmsman, because the boat was too heavily loaded, steered towards the West Bank to avoid the wind and waves. Unexpectedly, the bottom of the boat hit a stone embankment, breaking a large hole. Instantly, the cabin flooded, and the boat sank immediately. The passengers, crew, and others, a total of seven people, fell into the sea with the boat. They swam to escape for their lives. When they were near the shore, they were fortunately rescued by people. Six of the crew and passengers were able to survive. However, the boat owner, Shi Hongchun, 24 years old, tragically drowned on the spot. His body has not yet been recovered. After the crew and others were rescued, they immediately reported to Xu Jinji in Song. After hearing the report, the head of the tax firm, Xu Xigeng, immediately hired a small tugboat to go to the scene of the accident and tried to salvage the sunken boat and tow it to Yuncao Creek. It was found that most of the vegetables loaded had been lost, and the boat was also severely damaged. The loss of the boat and cargo was very large. The crew has already reported the situation to the boat owner and is waiting for the boat owner's wife to come to Shanghai to deal with it. It is said that the boat owner's wife is only 19 years old. Upon hearing this bad news, it was like a bolt from the blue. The tragic situation is beyond description.

Stock Broker Swindles 60,000 Yuan in Treasury Bonds; Yuan Qinsun Sentenced to Three Months in Prison

Yuan Qinsun, a native of Ningbo, was a broker at the Dingyu Securities Firm at No. 413 Zhaofu Lane, Hankou Road. Recently, due to economic pressure and heavy debts, he came up with a whimsical idea, falsely claiming that Dunyu Qianzhuang (a money shop) wanted to purchase twelve 20-year Salt Tax Treasury Bonds, with a face value of 5,000 yuan each, totaling 60,000 yuan, worth 27,000 yuan at market price. The owner of the firm, Liu Yunpan, believed him to be true and purchased twelve Treasury Bonds from the stock exchange. On the 29th of last month, he handed the bonds to Yuan to be delivered to Dunyu Qianzhuang. Unexpectedly, after Yuan obtained the bonds,

he disappeared without a trace. Liu became suspicious and inquired with Dunyu, and found that there was no such transaction. He immediately reported it to the General Police Station, requesting an investigation. Detectives Han Shoushan and Wu Yaozu went to Yuan's residence at No. 19 Fansheng Lane, Xihua Road, to arrest him. Unexpectedly, Yuan had moved his entire family to another location on the 25th, and his whereabouts were unknown. However, according to his roommate, Yuan had hired a moving company truck to move his furniture at that time. The detectives then investigated various moving companies and learned that the Zhoujiazu Road China Moving Company had transported the furniture to No. 46 Mintiniyin Road in the French Concession. The detectives went to the address and arrested Yuan, confiscating the stolen Treasury Bonds. One bond had already been sold, netting 2,100 yuan. After spending 200 yuan, he deposited 1,200 yuan, and the rest was cash, all of which was confiscated by the detectives and taken back to the police station. Yesterday morning, he was escorted to the First Special Court Criminal Division. Police lawyer Zhang Shizhu stated the circumstances and requested that he be punished according to law for the crime of embezzlement. When Yuan was questioned, he confessed without denial. Qian Hongye, the Criminal Division Judge, verified the confession and immediately announced the judgment in court: Yuan Qinsun committed fraud to obtain property and was sentenced to three months in prison as a warning.

Case of a Pedestrian Killed by a Falling Tree; | Appeal Hearing Today |

Chen Ronggui, 38 years old, a native of Suzhou, resided in the old schoolyard in the new north gate of the South City in Shanghai, and worked at the German company Meyer & Co. on Guangdong Road in the Public Concession. On May 12th of this year at 5:00 PM, after finishing his work, he was returning home. While walking in front of the old Jiatai Tea Shop at No. 46 Laobeimen Street in the French Concession, a giant wooden log, more than ten feet long, suddenly fell from the roof of the third floor of the shop, hitting him in the head. He was rushed to Renji Hospital for treatment, but died due to his serious injuries. The court examined the body. The tea shop's staff came to the case and admitted that it was indeed the wooden log falling from the roof of the shop that caused the death. The deceased's 67-year-old mother, Chen Zhang, and his wife, Chen Huang, filed a criminal lawsuit with the Second Special Court, claiming that he left behind a family of ten men, women, old and young, whose future life was dependent. They requested that the defendants be punished according to law and, incidentally, a civil lawsuit, and that they be ordered to compensate for all relevant losses. Unexpectedly, the deceased's wife, Chen Huang, became ill and gave birth to a stillborn child due to grief over her husband's tragic death. After the Second Special Court summoned the case for cross-examination, it initially only ordered both parties to attempt reconciliation. Then, it judged the defendant not guilty. The plaintiff was not satisfied, and Chen Zhang and others still hired lawyer Zhu Gaorong to file an appeal with the Third Branch of the Jiangsu High Court. The reasons for his rebuttal were several. According to the reporter's knowledge, the main points were roughly that "the giant wood was placed on the roof, according to the defendant's confession, for more than a year." "On the day of the accident, there was a strong wind, blowing down the giant wood. The plaintiff produced a handwritten certificate from the director of the Xujiahui Observatory, stating that there was no wind at all that day." They requested that justice be served. It is known that the Third Branch of the High Court, after receiving the petition, scheduled to summon the plaintiff and defendant to the case for trial at 3:00 PM today.

Shop Assistant Stabbed, Shop Owner Hangs Himself

Shen Linghua, a local man, (34 years old) who lived at No. 21 Yaojia Stone Bridge, Qiuzhen East, Zhabei, and opened a garment shop, had a shop assistant, Du Linsheng, stabbed several times by a thug who broke into Shen's house through the back window at 2:00 AM the day before yesterday. He bled profusely and fell to the ground. He was rushed to the Sacred Heart Hospital on Ningguo Road in the Public Concession for treatment. It is now learned that the garment shop owner, Shen Linghua, suddenly hanged himself from a tree near Yaojia Stone Bridge at 4:00 PM the day before yesterday. The matter is quite bizarre. After the police station of the Third Section of the Fifth District of the Municipal Public Security Bureau learned of the incident, they reported it to the director, Wen Yishan, who in turn reported it to the General Bureau. They immediately sent a patrol officer to investigate and ordered the local guarantor to request the court to send a prosecutor to examine the body yesterday.

Two Bank Inspection Reports

The Central Bank's 180th Report on Issuance Reserve: This committee, according to Article 15 of the Central Bank Regulations, is responsible for inspecting the reserve fund for the bank's issuance of convertible notes. We conducted the 180th inspection at the bank's Issuance Bureau on November 30, the 22nd year of the Republic of China. The results of the inspection are announced as follows: (A) Total issuance of convertible notes: 69,119,130 silver dollars, including 63,328,331 silver dollar notes and 5,790,799 fractional currency notes. Total convertible note reserve: 69,119,130 silver dollars, including: Cash reserve of 56,421,130 silver dollars, of which 53,065,284 silver dollars are stored in the bank's issuance vault, 1,554,180 silver dollars are deposited in branches in various ports, and 1,800,666 silver dollars are deposited with other banks. Guarantee reserve converted to 12,698,000 silver dollars. (B) Total issuance of Customs Gold Unit convertible notes: 416,715.40 Customs Gold Units. Total Customs Gold Unit convertible note reserve: 416,715.40 Customs Gold Units. This reserve includes 6,995 taels and 3.9 mace of bullion, valued at 5,957, equivalent to 416,715.40 Customs Gold Units. According to Article 2 of the Central Bank's convertible note regulations, the cash reserve is 60% and the guarantee reserve is 40%. The inspection results show that the cash exceeds 60% and the guarantee is less than 40%, which is in compliance with the regulations. This report is hereby issued. November 30, the 22nd year of the Republic of China. Chairman of the Supervisory Committee of the Central Bank, Li Fuxun, Supervisors Xie Mingdong, Qin Runqing, Yu Qiaqing, Lin Kanghou, Xu Jiyu.

The Bank of China's Inspection Report on Issuance Reserve: The Bank of China's issuance of convertible notes and reserve fund for November of the 21st year have now been inspected by supervisors Chuan Qilin and He Shaoyin, Xie Jishan, together with accountant Xu Yongzuo, on December 1. The inspection results are listed separately below. Total issuance of convertible notes: 11,618,610 yuan. Total reserve fund: 11,618,610 yuan, including cash reserve of 7,532,110 yuan, more than 60%, and guarantee reserve of 4,086,500 yuan, less than 40%, which is in compliance with the issuance regulations.

Wireless Weekly

Wireless Machines of 1950

— Translated by Yizhi

Hugo Gernsback, editor-in-chief of the two major wireless magazines in the United States, Radio Craft and Short Wave Craft, is a polymath and quite famous in the wireless field. He recently published an article on the Radio Set of 1950 in Radio Craft magazine. Although it is a prediction and may not be reliable, it is based on his rich experience and excellent knowledge and speculation. It cannot be compared with a generation of empty generalizations. After reading this article, I was quite interested, so I excerpted the translation for the wireless comrades in our country to see. We will wait and see, or will we feel emotional and strive to catch up? — Translator's Note.

In the past few months, I have often been asked by Radio Craft readers what my guesses are about future wireless machines. I have made many predictions, and some have been accurate. At this time when the wireless machine industry is in a slump, I am afraid that the wireless comrades will not be surprised by what they want to know about the future wireless machines.

I believe that the future wireless machines in my speculation will not be too far away. However, I do not believe that they can be seen next year or within five years. When can this machine be seen? The earliest is probably in the early autumn of 1950.

The radio of 1950 is not a small, cigar box-style or pocket-sized one. This machine must be at least four feet high or higher. Because it can also receive wireless movies and has a screen, it must be very large.

The vacuum tubes inside the machine are heatless or electrodeless. The area is very small, I am afraid that it is not as large as a finger ring.

The machine base will be very different from today's. The parts (transformers, etc.) will not be fixed for the convenience of rapid repair. The installation method is like the current installation of vacuum tubes. They can be removed immediately. The sockets are like today's vacuum tube sockets or like bayonets. With just a twist of the wrist, the transformer or capacitor to be removed can be taken out. I have heard current engineers say that if the wiring is not firmly fixed, nothing can be heard except for bad noise. However, of the vacuum tubes, which are now called the soul of the wireless machine, which one is soldered? Therefore, in manufacturing, if the contact points are properly worked on in the arrangement, there will definitely be no difficult problems.

The vacuum tube itself has a more complicated structure and higher efficiency than today's. At that time, the real detection tube will definitely have been invented. Its efficiency will definitely be better than today's, and the sensitivity will definitely be increased several times as a percentage. Therefore, the 1950 machine does not need an antenna, does not need a ground wire, and external noise and static interference can be reduced. Each machine will be equipped with a correct filter brush丨not the filter used today, it can reduce the interference noise from the current power input line from 90% to 95%.

The loudspeakers on future machines will also be different from today's. Instead of magnetic or electric, they will use mineral or capacitor types, or a combination of the two. The 1950 machine will have many loudspeakers, each responsible for a certain fixed audio frequency, so that the high and low tones can be as realistic as the original sound.

In 1950, the current broadcast wavelength bands will all be cancelled. The broadcasting wavelength rate is below 200 meters. At that time, if wireless movies are successful, then the current broadcast wavelengths will be useless. The wireless movie broadcast wavelength is below 50 meters, and each station uses the same wavelength to broadcast both image and sound. This has been mentioned in my editor's notes, and in April 1932, the New York station of the Columbia Broadcasting System had completed the simultaneous broadcast of sound and image.

Future wireless movies will definitely make great progress. The broadcasting distance will be long, the lens will be clear, and the human figures will be realistic. All broadcasting stations will be able to broadcast color wireless movies. All can be received with the 1950 machine. The cheapest broadcasting machine broadcasts black and white. Good ones can broadcast the three primary colors of red, blue, and yellow, and various colors mixed from them.

The 1950 machine will all be made of all metal. To avoid external electrical interference, the entire machine will be sealed with metal. The back of the machine will not be opened like today, causing dust to enter.

Electromagnetic Rectifier

— Li Yuanqing

The sole mission of a rectifier is to convert alternating current (AC) into unidirectional direct current (DC). Currently, vacuum tube rectifiers are perhaps the most commonly used. Another type, called electrolytic rectifiers, is not widely used due to their large size and inconvenience for carrying.

The rectifier introduced in this article utilizes the electromagnetic principle of "like charges repel, opposite charges attract." The content is very simple and suitable for small-scale experiments. As shown in the first figure, M is a horseshoe permanent magnet, and V is a thin iron piece. When alternating current passes through the coil C, V becomes an electromagnet due to induction, with the same frequency as the alternating current (each cycle changes the north and south poles once; for example, if the frequency is 60, the north and south poles each change 60 times per second). Assuming that in a certain cycle, the A terminal of the upper half-cycle is the south pole (S), then S repels S, and at the same time, S is attracted to N on the left. Thus, the current generated by S2 (the secondary coil of the power transformer) can pass through at point X (see Figure 2A). In the lower half-cycle, the A terminal becomes the north pole (N), then N repels N, and N attracts S, so point X separates, and the current cannot pass through (see Figure 2B). As a result, the obtained half-wave unidirectional current is the same as that rectified by a diode vacuum tube (as shown in the curve).

In Figure 1, T is a doorbell transformer, and the secondary coil S1 is specifically for the current in the C coil. S2 is a 5-volt secondary coil. After rectification, if charging a 4-volt A battery, a current of about 2 amps can be obtained.

This article only describes the principle, and all sections are simplified. If the reader wants to expand the use of this device, such as charging A batteries with a large amount of current or B batteries with higher voltage, they only need to modify the power transformer. The other parts do not need to be moved. For detailed design of the power transformer, please refer to issues 9 and 10 of this publication.

Such electromagnetic rectifiers are also sold on the market, but most are fake. Buyers should pay attention.

Note: The DC voltage obtained after rectification must be higher than the battery's own voltage when there is no load for it to be applicable. For example, the voltage of a B battery should be around 45 volts. In short, when winding the secondary coil of the transformer, it is better to have more turns than fewer. If the voltage is too high, a resistor of appropriate value can be connected in series to adjust it. If it is too low, it must be unwound and rewound.

Construction of a Mechanical Rectifier

— Shi Huayu

Charging requires a large amount of direct current. Besides DC generators, what is sold on the market is AC-to-DC chargers. Among homemade ones, mechanical rectifiers are the most suitable.

AA is a round soft iron bar, 25 mm in diameter and 100 mm long, wound with 1000 turns of #30 enameled wire, with wax paper insulation between each layer. #30 wire can pass a current of 0.067 amps, so a 300-ohm resistor is used to limit the current passing through. N is a piece of steel strip with strong magnetism, 10 mm wide and about 60 mm long, the thinner the better. A watch spring with magnetization can also be used. E is the fixed point of the steel strip. C is a small screw to adjust the distance between B and D. D is a triangular iron block, fixed on a wooden board for contact. F is a fuse. After all the wires are connected according to the diagram, it can be used. When alternating current passes through the coil along the dotted line arrow, a magnetic field is generated around it. According to the right-hand rule, the A end should be the north pole and A' the south pole. At the same time, because the end of the steel strip B close to A is the north pole, it is attracted, so it touches D. Thus, there is current passing through the RSD circuit, with the direction indicated by the curve arrow. Conversely, if the alternating current flows in the direction of the solid line arrow, the A end generates north pole magnetism and repels the steel strip B, so point D does not make contact, and there is no current passing through the RSD circuit. The direction of the alternating current changes constantly, so there is a constantly flowing, intermittently flowing, unidirectional current in the RSD circuit, thus completing the rectification process. The amount of direct current needed can be adjusted with R. If there is a suitable filtering device, it can also be used in place of a B battery or an A battery.

Simple Method for Measuring Capacitance

— Lu Qing

Measuring the capacitance of a capacitor requires a precise electrical meter. However, such meters are very expensive, and most amateurs do not have them. Therefore, homemade capacitors or those whose capacitance has been forgotten are often difficult to use in circuits because their capacitance cannot be determined. The method introduced here also does not require an electrical meter. The equipment used and the required procedures are very simple, making it suitable for amateurs. The circuit diagram is as follows.

In the diagram, V is a triode vacuum tube, T is an ordinary low-frequency transformer, P is its primary, S is its secondary, the A battery is at the specified value, the B battery can be arbitrary, R1 and R2 are two parts of a wire-wound potentiometer, C1 is a capacitor with known capacitance, H is a headset, and C2 is the capacitor to be measured.

During measurement, first adjust the potentiometer so that no sound is heard in the headset. At this point, the resistance and capacitance are related by the formula C1 × R1 = C2 × R2. Since R1, R2, and C1 are known values, the capacitance of C2 can be directly calculated using the formula C2 = (C1 × R1) ÷ R2.

If a 600-ohm potentiometer and a 2000-ohm headset are used with the above method to measure capacitors with a capacitance less than 0.005 MF, the measured value will not be very accurate. However, if a more sensitive headset and a potentiometer with a larger resistance are used, even capacitors with smaller capacitances can be measured. Using a higher-frequency low-frequency oscillator or increasing the B voltage can also achieve the same effect.

Note: If the circuit described in this article is not in use, the vacuum tube must be removed, or a switch must be added to the filament circuit to avoid wasting current. (Translated from the November issue of Radio Craft).

Crystal Loudspeaker

— Chongwu

Recently, there is a new type of loudspeaker that uses oscillating crystals to convert electrical energy into sound waves. This type of loudspeaker is different from ordinary types in that it does not have a magnet inside, relying entirely on the unique properties of crystals to work. A long time ago, radio engineers already knew about this phenomenon, that is, when a Rochelle Salt crystal is placed in an electrostatic magnetic field, oscillations immediately occur. This unique function is called the Piezoelectric effect, and it is now used to create effective loudspeakers.

In appearance, this loudspeaker is similar to the dynamic type, but the transformer and heavy magnet inside the dynamic type are replaced in the crystal loudspeaker by a very simple hollow circular chamber. Inside the chamber is a finely ground Rochelle Salt crystal, shaped like a small square, with three corners held in place by rubber clips, and the remaining corner is free to move, connected to the sound arm of the conical horn. In addition, two thin copper sheets are attached to both sides of the crystal to form two poles. When the pulsating current from the low-frequency amplifier in the radio is applied to these two copper sheets, which are similar to capacitors, the crystal twists and bends, resulting in a series of oscillations. Through the action of the triangular rubber clips, these oscillations are transmitted to the horn through the sound arm to form sound waves.

Compared with magnetic induction and dynamic loudspeakers, crystal loudspeakers have several advantages. The most important is that their structure is simple and not prone to failure. And because no magnet is needed inside, they are light and convenient. For example, the loudspeaker shown in the figure below weighs only two pounds and is less than three and a half inches thick. The loudspeaker shown in the figure below is only driven by a simple crystal. There are also many other styles, especially designed to meet the needs of public speaking and theaters. Inside, there are four crystal pieces, connected to each other to drive a horn or diaphragm.

Another advantage of this crystal loudspeaker is that it is particularly suitable for dual-loudspeaker setups. When it works side by side with a dynamic loudspeaker, the result is much better than using two dynamic loudspeakers side by side. Therefore, by extension, they are also very worthy of being adopted when multiple loudspeakers need to work side by side!

Shi Huayu, taboo name Qibei, Wei Xinsu, Chun, Li Yuanqing, Weiyan, Zhu Ziyuan, Yizhi, Yun, Keming, Jiancun, RF, Chen Xianwen, Chungang, Gentlemen, please note that the manuscript fees for November can be collected from the accounting department of this museum from 2 pm to 4 pm on the 6th to 10th and 16th to 20th of this month, with the seal affixed to the manuscript.

Shenbao Radio Weekly Department

AC/DC Radio

— Cheng Quan

In recent years, more and more cities in the country are using alternating current, so AC radios can also be used in various places. However, except for a few large cities, most places do not have electricity supply, so AC radios are still not very suitable. If DC machines are used day and night, the procedures are extremely inconvenient and very uneconomical. The AC/DC dual-purpose machine described below can solve the above-mentioned difficulties. The circuit is very simple and suitable for homemade use. Those who are interested may wish to try it. In the figure, L1, L2, and L3 are ordinary three-circuit coils, and L4 is a center-tapped RFC for use, which can also be homemade. Use a one-inch tube to wind 800 turns of #36 wire, and tap a wire at 400 turns to connect to the crystal CD. The crystal must be purchased with the most sensitivity. The volume of this machine depends entirely on the quality of the crystal, and it must be fixed to avoid the trouble of adjustment. VC1 is an ordinary 21-plate variable capacitor. VC2 is a small 13-plate variable capacitor, used to adjust regeneration. T1 and T2 are 3:1 low-frequency transformers. V1, V2, and V3 are all RCA 201 (similar to Byrd 401 and Philips 509). C1 is a 0.002 fixed capacitor. C2 are each 2 MFD, and C3 is 1 MFD. HFC is a 30-henry low-frequency choke coil. The secondary of an ordinary low-frequency transformer can also be used as a substitute. R is 1500 ohms. R1 is a 6-ohm variable resistor, and R2 is a 200-ohm voltage divider. PT is a power transformer, which can also be homemade. S is a switch, and S1 is a triple-pole double-throw switch. Please pay attention to the following points when manufacturing:

(1) This circuit is a regenerative type.

Therefore, each component must be very good.

(2) The power supply must be placed separately from the radio to reduce noise.

(3) The primary of the power transformer must be determined according to the local voltage. If the voltage is not accurate, you must wind more taps to adjust it.

(4) Within 100 miles of the radio station, you can use a loudspeaker.

(5) If you want to increase the volume when using AC, V2 can be changed to RC112AA.

(6) Use a 6-volt 100-amp storage battery and a 90-volt dry battery for DC. If AC and DC are used interchangeably, it can be used for three or four months.

Common Sense

— Huang Jiancun

(20) Overview of Vacuum Tubes (4)

(7) AC Vacuum Tubes: The various vacuum tubes described previously are all DC types, which can be used in DC radios but not in AC radios. However, since the invention of AC vacuum tubes, the shortcomings of the past have been eliminated, and the speed of their development has been rapid, making today's era of all-powerful AC radios. Originally, old DC vacuum tubes (such as UX201) would often generate a kind of noise - commonly known as AC hum - when the A battery was removed and replaced with an A eliminator to supply AC from the lighting line to the vacuum tube filament, disrupting the correct sound and making it unusable. AC vacuum tubes improve the filament so that it can be used for AC without the risk of generating AC hum. This type of AC vacuum tube is divided into two types due to the different structures of the filament: directly heated AC tubes and indirectly heated AC tubes. The different structures are briefly described below.

(A) Directly Heated AC Tubes: The biggest cause of AC hum is the change in temperature and the change in the potential difference between the grid and the filament. Directly heated AC tubes improve these two phenomena to minimize their changes. The filament of the tube uses an oxide-coated material to increase its heat sensitivity, and the current is increased to reduce the supply voltage Ef, and the change in the potential difference between the grid and the filament is also minimized. Other parts are almost the same as DC tubes. For example, UX226 and UX245 are one type of directly heated tube, and the specifications of the UX226 tube are roughly the same as the DC tube UX201A, but its AC hum is reduced to one-tenth.

(B) Indirectly Heated AC Tubes: Indirectly heated tubes separate the two functions of the filament - heating and emission - so that they are performed separately. The part that performs the heating function is called the filament or heater, and the part that performs the emission function is called the cathode. For example, UY227 and UY224 are one type of indirectly heated tube. The above figure shows the structure of the heating part and the cathode.

(Nanjing, 1st) The Ministry of Education telegraphed to the educational bureaus of various provinces and cities on the 1st, stating that the interim regulations for the joint entrance examination for students in primary and secondary schools have been revised by the ministry. The revised regulations will be issued separately, and they should be strictly followed from the joint entrance examination of this semester. This order.

(60) Translation 1. Able to directly listen to lectures in a foreign language or Esperanto; 2. Able to write a short letter in a foreign language or Esperanto; 3. Able to translate a piece of foreign text or Esperanto.

(61) Guiding 1. Familiar with the streets, shortcuts, back alleys, and bridges within approximately four kilometers of the troop headquarters; 2. Able to guide on local routes day and night and indicate the direction of neighboring villages and towns; 3. Familiar with the detailed addresses and telephone numbers of well-known doctors, hospitals, public security bureaus, fire brigades, telephone and telegraph offices, post offices, stations, car and bicycle rental places, public places, fire alarm tables, etc., near the troop headquarters, as well as the routes of railways, buses, and trams; 4. Know the special products of the hometown; 5. Know the historical outline, famous scenic spots, and historical sites of the hometown.

(62) Painting 1. Know the historical outline, characteristics, and trends of Chinese and Western painting; 2. Understand the general meaning of color ( ); 3. Know the painting methods of Chinese or Western painting, and be able to paint a memory painting, a sketch, a decorative painting, a propaganda painting, and a current affairs satirical painting each.

(63) Climbing 1. Able to perform temporary lookout work; 2. Know the steps for going up and down mountains; 3. Able to climb over rope frames higher than seven meters; 4. Able to climb mountains in the dark or in wind, rain, ice, and snow; 5. Able to cross rivers or valleys using ropes or rattan; 6. Able to climb hanging ropes, trees, and masts higher than six meters; 7. Able to find ways to overcome obstacles.

(64) Veterinary Medicine 1. Know the essentials of anatomy; 2. Know the living habits and feeding methods of domestic animals; 3. Able to implement conditioning methods after domestic animals have been injured or abused.

(65) Bookkeeping 1. Able to do modern bookkeeping and apply account statements; 2. Familiar with commercial arithmetic; 3. Know the differences, advantages, and disadvantages of Chinese and Western bookkeeping; 4. Proficient in using abacus and computers; 5. Know the general meaning of accounting.

(66) Photography 1. Know the principles of photography; 2. Know the structure and usage of lenses and camera boxes; 3. Able to photograph five landscape photos (including two scenes, snow scenes, and night scenes), three portrait photos, three still life photos, two interior scene photos, and two moving object photos, which must be developed, printed, and mounted, and the photography location, time, light, lens aperture, shutter speed, film, development method, and printing paper must be indicated.

(67) Debate 1. Able to give a speech in Mandarin for more than five minutes and prepare a concise summary of the speech in advance; 2. Know the rules of debate and understand the powers of the chairman; 3. Able to serve as the affirmative and negative sides in debates each more than twice, with a total score of 60 points; 4. Know the actions, attitude, and other points that should be noted during the debate.

Able to make a week-long camping or sailing plan for a small team of Boy Scouts; 5. Travel long distances by boat or car for more than three days, with a daily itinerary of more than 15 kilometers, and know the luggage that needs to be carried; 6. Have camped outdoors or on a boat for more than two weeks; 7. Know how to make fire without matches, how to filter drinking water, and other necessary common sense; 8. Able to lead a small team of Boy Scouts for outdoor living practice; 9. Able to make a report on camping experience or insights.

(69) Mining 1. Know the general situation of minerals in this country and other countries; 2. As such, in addition to separate orders, this order is hereby issued to inform the bureau and to inform all subordinates.

Education Association The Municipal Education Association notified all districts, stating that the Municipal Anti-Rebellion Citizens' Congress will be held at the Public Sports Field on Daji Road at 2:00 pm on December 2. At that time, all executive officers of your district must be present, and all members must be notified to attend.

Municipal Education Bureau Reprimands Taihu Middle School for Establishing Junior High School Without Authorization, Which is Illegal, and Orders the Cancellation of the Second and Third Grade Classes

The Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau yesterday issued an order to the Private Taihu Junior Middle School and Primary School, stating that according to the complaint filed by Min Danwei, the founder of the school, the school's management is improper and the measures are erroneous, and he requested to resign as the founder. The bureau has sent personnel to investigate, and the report briefly stated that, in general, there are many students in the school, and five private houses are rented. There is no open space nearby, which is quite crowded. The light in the classrooms is mostly unsuitable, and the spirit of the teachers in class is not active, and their abilities are weak. Regarding the consumer cooperative and the school accounts, they cannot be publicly distributed, which seems inappropriate. There are complaints about the female teacher Ying in the outside world, so it is advisable to order the school board to find a way to rehire. The junior high school has been opened for less than a year, and it has illegally recruited second and third grade students, so it should be severely reprimanded and ordered to be corrected to comply with the law. Based on this, the junior high school has not been reported to the bureau for record, and it has been established without authorization. It has been opened for less than a year, and it has recruited second and third grade students without authorization, which are all violations of laws and regulations and should be reprimanded. The school must immediately follow the prescribed procedures to apply for establishment and cancel the second and third grade classes. The school must report for verification, otherwise it will be banned. New Construction of the Physical Education Department of the Patriotic Girls' School

Qingyuan, Jiangwan Road, is very beautiful and has a peaceful atmosphere, which is suitable for reading and sports. The Physical Education Department of the Patriotic Girls' School is located here. The department has a long history and has long been known for its reputation. The January 28th Incident suffered a heavy blow. After the war, Li Jiyuan from Beiping was specially hired as the director to actively revive it. On the occasion of the school's 32nd anniversary today, the past situation and future plans of the department are described in detail below:

Historical Evolution The Physical Education Department was added by the school in the third year of the Republic of China. At the beginning, Mr. McLelland, an American physical education expert, was hired to plan everything. The purpose was to cultivate female physical education teachers for primary and secondary schools. The initial duration of study was half a year. In the eighth year of the Republic of China, it was changed to two years, and in the nineteenth year, it was changed to a three-year system. Graduates who serve society are all over the country and abroad. In the past national games, provincial games, and the Far Eastern Games held in Shanghai, the department participated in group performances and won honors. Dance, national arts, volleyball, basketball, and track and field events also have good results. The Girls' Junior Army was also the first to be founded by the school in the country (in the eighth year of the Republic of China). The current commander is Ms. Huang Shan. The honor of this grand review and grand camp is a sincere matter.

Overview of Revival After the war, it moved back to its original site and rebuilt its foundation. The outline is as follows: A. Equipment (1) The gymnasium is completed, 70 feet long and 40 feet wide, suitable for women's basketball court. It is equipped with volleyball and softball fields. The equipment includes ribbed bars, horizontal bars, parallel bars, hanging ladders, hanging ropes, hanging wooden horses, jumping boxes, handstand racks, balance beams, chest expanders, springboards, etc., all of which are complete. The attached changing rooms, storage rooms, and storage rooms are also very complete. (2) The increase in sports fields. The track and field track is 180 meters long around the perimeter. Jumping pits, iron ball circles, etc. are all complete. All kinds of sports are very suitable. The lawn tennis court and hard tennis court are well arranged and suitable for winter and summer. The new dormitory is equipped with a handball court, and the South Courtyard is equipped with a basketball and volleyball court. With this equipment, the Physical Education Department of the Shanghai Girls' School has benefited a lot in teaching.

Curriculum The curriculum of the department is revised according to the needs of the society and the physical education normal school curriculum standards promulgated by the Ministry of Education. For technical subjects, the Technical Subjects Teaching Materials Committee separately formulates a technical subject teaching material outline and a technical subject testing standard. The outline and testing standard will be published in the physical education quarterly magazine compiled by the department for research with modern physical education experts.

Implementation of Teaching The department is now divided into three classes. The courses are taught with strictness, life emphasizes discipline, and attention is paid to the cleanliness of the residence, the neatness of the uniform, and extracurricular exercise. Lectures, parties, reading clubs and other activities are all presided over by the student self-government association and are guided and supervised by the director. Regarding gymnastics, Mr. Chen Fen is currently teaching it, and the lessons are rigorous. In just a few months, he has achieved remarkable results. The school's physical education focuses on popularity. Morning exercises are divided into three types: ordinary exercises, track and field sports, and Taijiquan. Principal Sun is particularly good at teaching Taijiquan.

Three-Year Plan Director Li of the department formulated a three-year plan at the beginning of the revival. The results that are currently being announced are the success of the first year plan. The plan is published below: First Year Plan: Construction and Consolidation 1. Stipulate the steps and budget of the three-year plan; 2. Revise the curriculum organization; 3. Formulate various regulations; 4. Compile a curriculum outline; 5. Formulate a technical subject teaching material outline; 6. Formulate technical subject testing standards; 7. Organize a promotion committee to plan all promotion matters; 8. Publish a physical education magazine; 9. Organize a physical education school teaching material research association; 10. Consolidate and implement the physical education organization of the middle school department; 11. Implement discipline; 12. Add a gymnasium, exercise field, ball field, etc.; 13. Expand the existing exercise field, ball field, etc.; 14. Review and adopt various teaching materials; 15. Stipulate extracurricular assignment methods; 16. Stipulate scholarship methods. Second Year Plan: Enrichment and Research 1. Continue the work of the first year; 2. Revise and improve items 1, 2, 3, 4, 5, and 6 of the first year; 3. Expand the track and field field; 4. Rebuild the bathroom and changing room; 5. Raise funds to build a swimming pool; 6. Add a tennis court; 7. Increase the number of free places; 8. Select athletes to go to various places to compete and investigate the physical education conditions in various places; 9. Apparatus gymnastics performance; 10. Other performance items; 11. Enrich all content; 12. Improve school health implementation; 13. Organize a medical team; 14. Study the physical problems of women; 15. Handle all plans for the past two years. Third Year Plan: Improve the Level 1. Continue the work of the first and second years; 2. Improve the level and prepare for specialist courses; 3. Hire experts to design; 4. Study specialist courses; 5. Study national health and our country's inherent physical education; 6. Proceed and prepare all necessary conditions for specialist courses; 7. Proceed with specialist course establishment procedures; 8. Raise specialist course funds; 9. Prepare for specialist course enrollment matters; 10. The swimming pool is completed.

Recent Developments at the Shanghai Sports Association

Mr. Knie, a Czech national and world-renowned sports figure with various honorary trophies, has been running the Knie Sports School in Shanghai for over ten years, diligently striving for improvement. It was once reorganized into the Huang Ke Gymnasium. It is now heard that, in order to expand its business, it has been reorganized into the Shanghai Sports Association by Mr. Spielmann, a director of the Banque Franco-Chinoise, and others. Everything inside has been reorganized with great effort, making it look brand new, a far cry from the past. On the evening of the 28th, a banquet was held at the Green Pearl Hall of the Great Eastern Hotel to entertain fellow journalists and invite them to visit. It is said that the organization of the association is very complete. In addition to Mr. Spielmann as a committee member and Mr. Yu Hongjun, secretary of the municipal government, joining as a sponsor and member, other committee members include Dr. O'Hara, lawyer Li Zhongdao, Guo Baoshu, Chen Gaocong, and Westerners such as Mr. Lai Haoshi. Mr. Knie remains as the sports director, providing instructions on everything. In addition to a great gym, massage room, and bathroom, there is also a very complete library. In short, the facilities are hard to find in Shanghai compared to other clubs. It is also said that the membership fee is very low, and significant results can be achieved after practicing for a certain period of time to strengthen the body, lose weight, and build muscle. The association's regulations are printed and available upon request. The association is located at No. 888 Weihaiwei Road, at the intersection of Seymour Road, telephone number 34607.
