Spring and Autumn

Increasing Population

— Hua Ling

"There are three unfilial acts, the greatest of which is to have no descendants." "Nowadays, even though they are busy" "repairing the Confucius Temple" and "advocating the reading of classics," this kind of "anti-feminist" ancient teaching still does not produce much reproductive power and cannot match the popularity of "Birth Control Guidance" and "Practical Contraception." Unexpectedly, in this "century of birth control," countries are actually advocating for the effort to create little citizens. It's really interesting.

Italy, since the implementation of Fascism, has long been known for its "reproduction policy" in order to expand its national power. For example, the government provides annual subsidies for living expenses to those who have a certain number of children, and the government awards medals to those who have a certain number of children. News about such things is often recorded in newspapers. Recently, the new tricks have become more and more exciting. On the day of the marriage festival organized by the Fascist Party, more than two thousand couples in Rome held weddings. Each couple received a portrait of the Prime Minister, five hundred Italian lire, and sugared almonds. Moreover, the church also joined in the fun, willing to give the first child born to these two thousand newlywed couples a special honor that is not easily obtained. Oh, marrying a wife and having children has so many benefits, who wouldn't try their best? Only a fool wouldn't.

Italy's comrade, Germany, has also recently been working hard to promote the reproduction of the superior Germanic race. According to the statistics released by Dr. Bergdolt of the German Bureau of Statistics, if Germans do not work hard to produce children and maintain a sufficient population output rate, then, based on the population decline rate in the past seventy years, the population will fall to one-fortieth within five generations. This alarming theory has naturally given the Germans, who are known far and wide for their patriotism, a youthful shift and a powerful stimulant. If our Elder Brother Xi shouts from a high place again, why worry that every household will not hold a baby shower next year on this day?

Take Soviet Russia for example, without talking about any ethnicity, but it is said that in order to increase revolutionary power, they have also closed their doors and encouraged the people to work hard to create future warriors for the government. Except for those due to physiological reasons, abortion is a great crime. In addition to children born to formal couples, illegitimate children are also recognized by law. After all is said and done, this is nothing more than to increase the population. As for our eastern neighbor, they regard increasing the population as equally important as expanding military preparedness. No one can deny that.

Judging from the global trend, "having no descendants" is not only unfilial, but simply "disloyal." Therefore, I advise modern bachelors who are unwilling to be out of step with the times to quickly place marriage advertisements in newspapers and choose an auspicious day to get married. Married couples, quickly eat "seed elixirs" as meals, so as to keep trying again and again, working hard for the country.

Happy

— Ding Ming

I have been bathing in that bathhouse for two or three years, and I'm used to it. Although my life has changed several times in the past two or three years, regardless of the distance, regardless of winter, summer, spring, or autumn, I go there nineteen times out of ten. I don't know what day it was, but a short and vigorous young man suddenly smiled and shamelessly called me "Happy"! So every time I went, they would all smile and call me "Oh! Happy!" or say, "Ah! Happy is here again!"

As for me? I found it very interesting. While dealing with them, I thought to myself, "Alas! Happy? What a beautiful synonym! But happy about what? Alone and adrift, living in this world, without the beautiful environment that people have, studying and seeking advanced knowledge, what is there to be happy about? And without the large amount of wealth that people have, able to use it as they please, appropriately, what is there to gain?"

However, they always call out. Not only when I arrive, but also when I leave, they still call out, "Oh! Happy is gone!"

The good thing about that bathhouse is that the towels and bath mats are always kept clean, and the service is extremely attentive. I'm used to it, often using their cleansing sponges unconditionally, and often chatting about everything. They have frank, straightforward, sincere, and consistent personalities and expressions. Other than what they deserve, they have no excessive demands. At first, I felt that their place was a smooth path in life. In my heart, I couldn't wait to bathe there every day, just to see them often and be happy! Later, I thought that these people were no different from wood and stone, only knowing themselves and not knowing others; only knowing how to serve society for their own food and clothing, and not knowing how to serve society for the broad masses. It was exactly as the Grand Historian Sima Qian said, "The common people are selected by themselves!" Because of this, I unconsciously felt a bit unhappy with them! But they are always better than those who obtain things without labor and are subject to legal sanctions, so I still like to associate with them!

Since I often go to that bathhouse, I can almost draw the interior layout: like that gold-painted price list, those pairs of bathing Western nude girls with beautiful curves, that declaration form for stepping on feet and bleeding, official seats, special seats, ordinary seats... most prominently, a couplet: "Double reflections in the waves, red leaves, the sun is bright / Phoenix perches on the pond, green algae, smoke hangs"

Happy goes, happy comes, coming and going, it's all happy. Today is truly happy, so I wrote this essay as a byproduct. Perhaps it is a scene in the city!

Lament for Jiangwan

— Huang Yingdai

Because I had to attend the unveiling ceremony of the Prime Minister's bronze statue, I got up early and took a car to the Chamber of Commerce. Walking across the Henan Road Bridge, the wind blowing in my face made me feel the early winter weather. On the bridge, during the morning rush hour, all those walking around were coolies and beggars. I only saw rickshaws and no cars. Compared to the cars and people of both genders mixed together at noon, they were clearly divided into two different social classes.

We were supposed to depart at eight o'clock, but we didn't set off until nine o'clock. Had I known this, why would I have gotten up early? Ah! This is the Chinese way! I'm really an idiot! A dozen or so trucks that usually carry goods were loaded with one or two thousand people: men, women, adults, and youths, all mixed together. Of course, I was one of them.

After passing the North Railway Station and leaving the bustling city, the convoy of trucks began to enter the Baoshan Road, where the yin wind was blowing and the ghostly atmosphere was heavy. The North Railway Station, which had been destroyed by artillery fire, had been repaired, making it impossible to see the traces of the war. However, the broken walls and rubble on Baoshan Road were still a sad sight. The bustling city of the past now only had a field of rubble. "Baoshan Road will not flourish again if the Commercial Press is not rebuilt." "That Oriental Library, the only cultural institution in China, was most regrettably destroyed by artillery fire!" "There are still remnants of yellow chrysanthemums here. It used to be a garden, but now only a desolate field remains!" As we passed the remains of the Commercial Press and the Oriental Library, we spoke in a disorderly manner, one sentence after another.

After the convoy passed Baoshan Road, we arrived at Jiangwan Road. The scenery here changed again. On the wasteland, scattered low houses stood on it without any order. Was this not also a battlefield! Burnt and bombed, the incomplete broken houses were often visible to you. This was indeed the method of clever people. If a house that had been bombed had not completely collapsed, cover it with boards and stack bricks into short walls. You didn't even have to pay rent. Many common people lived in these broken houses.

The wind blew in gusts. The national flag and the cold wind were in opposition, flapping in the breeze. Although the weather was very clear in the cold wind, I seemed to hear the ghosts of the patriots crying! This was their battlefield, their place of death. Our vehicles may have already run over their remains. It was because of our weakness that we could not avenge them, causing them to cry endlessly in the air!

Disappointing

— Xu Xiaoting

The higher the voice for promoting domestic goods, the more treacherous merchants selling enemy goods increase. These disappointing traitors simply have no national concept in their minds.

Parents are happiest with their clever children, but the more they like these children, the less they live up to their parents' expectations when they grow up.

Inland stores keep saying that there is no double price, but the disappointing clerks at the counter still do business with double prices.

The more corrupt officials are, the more they want to put on a façade of integrity. If they collapse one day, they don't blame themselves for not living up to the country's expectations, but blame their subordinates for not living up to their own expectations.

A beautiful wife with romantic habits, no matter how well you, as her husband, treat her, when she encounters the pursuit of the opposite sex, she doesn't ask whether her husband wants to wear a green hat or not, she doesn't live up to her husband's expectations.

Friends with a bad reputation like to boast about themselves when talking to others, but their disappointing reputation has already given the other party a considerable understanding and a considerable conclusion.

Four Northeast Company Commanders

— Zhang Henshui

Chapter 19: Wanting to Leave Yet Unable to, Recalling Past Events in the Same Car / Half Crying and Half Laughing, Leaning on a Pillow, Sick in the Decaying Autumn

Although Ji Zhi didn't say a word and only listened to others talking, after seeing the shadow of this building, his heart suddenly started to beat faster. Could it be that he would just take Gui Zhi home like this, section by section, and that would be the end of it? After taking her home, where would he go? Would he still wander around Haidian Street? Or would he sit in a milk tea shop for a while? Wandering around would be unconscious and afraid of running into acquaintances. But sitting in a milk tea shop? That would also be a joke. Entering the city from Dahongmen, taking the tram to Xizhimen, and then taking a long-distance bus from Xizhimen to Haidian, was it just to drink a bowl of sweet water in a milk tea shop? If none of that was possible, would he just take the original bus back? But the bus would have to drive to Xiangshan before driving back. There would be at least two or three hours of delay. Where could he settle himself for these two or three hours? With such hesitation in his heart, he couldn't help but show that sad look on his face. Gui Zhi thought to herself that it was her fault. He was kind enough to buy her a ticket and lead her onto the bus. From his expression, she knew that he only intended to return to Haidian to drop her off. Why was she giving him such a bad look? So she smiled at Ji Zhi and said, "When we get to Haidian, why don't you come up to our house for a seat?" Ji Zhi replied abruptly, "No need to go." He was originally just complaining. After saying it, he regretted it a bit. Why did he say "no need to go?" Gui Zhi only heard him say "no need to go." She had no idea that he was immediately regretting it in his heart. So she smiled and said, "Okay, see you another day." As she spoke, the bus had already stopped on Haidian Street. Gui Zhi followed the passengers and climbed down the bus. Ji Zhi jumped out of the bus and stood on the ground, patting the dust off his hands a few times. Gui Zhi, because he had taken her back from so far away, felt a little sorry for him just leaving like that. She stood to one side, watching him. (255)

Free Talk

Su Dongpo's Poetic Incarceration

— Zhu Xia

Su Dongpo was accused of writing poetry with satire, offending the court. On the day the incident occurred, he was still in office in Huzhou. Su Zhe received a secret report in Nanjing and urgently sent someone to inform Shi, so when Jingwei arrived in Huzhou, Shi had already asked for leave to visit his ancestors. Song Kong Pingzhong (Yi Fu) wrote about the situation at this time in "Tan Yuan": "Chuan (Huangfu Chuan, the Jing envoy) entered the state office directly, wearing robes and holding a tablet, standing in the courtyard, with two platform soldiers guarding him, dressed in white clothes and blue scarves, looking around evilly, the people's hearts were surging and unpredictable." In the end, he wrote a concluding remark with emotion, "In a blink of an eye, he pulled a prefect, like driving dogs and chickens. This matter was witnessed by Wupo (the current Quanzhou)." It is possible to imagine what Dongpo endured at that time. Later, his books were also banned, which I have already discussed in a previous article. Yesterday, I read Song Zhu Bian's (Shaozhang) "Feng Yue Tang Poetry Talk" and obtained very good information. The text reads:

Dongpo's poems and essays were immediately spread and recited by people. Every time a piece reached Lord Ou's office, he was happy all day long, and it was similar before and after. One day, while discussing essays with Fei, Lord Ou sighed and said, "Remember my words, thirty years later, the people of the world will not talk about me anymore." During the Chongning Daguan era, the overseas poetry saint was popular, and later generations no longer spoke of Lord Ou. At that time, although the court had tried to ban them, the rewards increased to 800,000, the ban became more severe, and the transmission became more and more, often boasting of having many. Scholars and officials who could not recite Dongpo's poems felt their spirits were exhausted, and some people called them uninspired. (Volume 1)

The influence of Dongpo's essays at that time, and the severity of the investigation, can be seen from this. "The stricter the ban, the more the transmission," the situation in ancient and modern times is exactly the same. The damage to Dongpo's spirit during the poetic incarceration was not small. When he was arrested and escorted to Beijing, he saw the ferocity of the arresting officers and thought it was a great disaster, so when he arrived at Taihu Lake, on a night when the wind and waves were surging and the moon was as beautiful as a painting, he actually wanted to jump into the water and commit suicide, but he canceled the idea for fear of implicating Su Zhe after his death. After being imprisoned in Beijing, he still thought he would die, and he had secretly prepared "Qingjin Dan" for suicide, and wrote poems to say goodbye to Zhe, including lines such as "I will repay my debts before my hundred years are over, and ten mouths have no support and burden people more," "I will be brothers with you for generations, and make an unfinished bond in the human world." However, although Dongpo suffered great damage to his spirit at this time, after he was released from prison, he actually relapsed and continued to write his poems, and privately scolded himself, "Still not changing." In fact, this unchanging is inevitable, because the oppression of punishment is ultimately not as painful as the bondage of the spirit.

Writing this, I remembered that in Song Han Qinglao Nong He Da's "Chun Zhu Ji Wen," there was also a story about banning Dongpo's essays. Since I have talked about poetic incarceration to banned books, I will copy this story together for people who study the banning of books in ancient and modern times to refer to. The text reads:

During the Shaosheng era, the court demoted and blamed the Yuan Yu ministers and banned and destroyed the academic writings of the Yuan Yu era. Some said that Sima Wen Gong's Shinto stele was written by Su Shi and should be removed and destroyed. Therefore, the state issued a decree to patrol and destroy the stele building and break the stele. Zhang Shanren heard this and said: "There is no need to send it like this. Just let the Shanren take a jade book official and add the words 'Not Appropriate' to the stele's title." The title of the stele originally said, "Stele of Loyalty, Purity, and Pure Virtue."

On Woodcuts

— Bai Shi

Some time ago, this column published two short articles discussing woodcuts, introducing several newly published woodcut picture books by Liangyou Bookstore. The popularity of woodcuts in China seems to be a recent phenomenon. It has been promoted by several bookstores (besides Liangyou, Modern also printed a thin volume of works by Chinese woodcut artists), the rise of woodcut research associations, and the publication in literary magazines, and supplements to translated collections, almost creating a small wave in Chinese literary circles.

Woodcut is an art that looks somewhat rigid, but it has a depth that other arts lack, like a clumsy person possessing rare advantages that a clever person does not have. It doesn't require any complicated colors, but relies solely on black and white to express moving and vivid images. Among many brother arts, it is the most lively, most open-minded, and strongest little brother. Its tools are just a few small knives, a piece of wood, and many sheets of paper for printing. It doesn't need to mix and stir colors directly on a palette like oil painting. However, although simple, carving requires profound artistic accomplishment and strong wrist strength. Of course, anyone who can draw a few strokes can scribble with a small knife, but I guarantee you won't carve anything good. Therefore, some people think that woodcut is a simple way to be popularized, but in reality, the production is still very sophisticated.

The main point of woodcut is strength, using brisk knife marks to carve vivid images. The method of woodcut is economy, reducing a large scene to a focal point, gathering a lot of "strength" to firmly gather in one place, the tighter it is compressed, the greater the "strength" it contains, and it is a top-notch work. Economy should be slightly exaggerated, for example, when carving a worker, his fists should be exaggerated to be very large -- of course, it should not be untrue -- larger than the head. As for metaphors like "chasing a person away like chasing a stray dog," it is also very important.

Because the main point is strength, woodcut is more suitable for carving figures, especially figures like laborers. Most of the woodcuts we see now are "rough people," which is the reason. The second is carving scenery, but the effectiveness of its characteristics is slightly reduced in scenery. From my personal point of view, I also feel that woodcut landscapes cannot surpass sketches or black and white paintings, although transplanting every grass and tree under the hard knives and pens is another kind of scene.

Abundance and Disaster

— Luo Hong

Liu Duo heard his companion’s cough, turned his head to take a look, and deliberately looked at the rice sacks in the cabin for a long time. For half an hour since the boat set sail, his eyes had often been on these rice sacks. This year's harvest really can't be considered bad. On average, each mu of land yielded two and a half shi. In the past few years, with such a harvest, he would really smile from ear to ear, row the boat to town to pay the rent, and when he came back, he could buy something. By the New Year, his daughter Xiao Mao and the others would have new cotton-padded jackets. Now that the harvest is good, Liu Duo is still worried every day. Isn't that so? The price of rice is much cheaper than in previous years. Even if each mu yields three shi, it is not as good as before. He sighed, and steering the rudder seemed to lack strength, looking far away at the place where the sky and the earth meet. His companion Qiu Tang coughed again, and he sighed and said:

"I calculated it over and over again, this year is the same as last year, another year of wasted effort!"

"You are much better than me. As for me, my own body is bad, and I hired someone to help. This year, I lost money again. By the New Year, I still have to borrow seventy or eighty yuan to pay Wang Daye's interest. This spring, I borrowed another hundred yuan from them, saying that the interest is one point three, and it's still looking at my acquaintance! Liu Duo, what are you worried about? As for me, if I think about it carefully, how can I live? I might as well hang myself. Do you know how much debt I have in total?…" Qiu Tang said, and coughed for a while.

Liu Duo spat hard, and the phlegm went backwards with a pile of garbage.

"These days are really strange. The price of rice has fallen so much, as if it were a time of peace. I heard the elders talk about the time when a bag of rice cost one yuan, and life was much better than now. Now, even though the price of rice has fallen, everyone says that life is hard."

A flock of birds was吵着 in the sky. Qiu Tang coughed again, without answering, just looking at the blue sky.

"The rent collectors are also shouting that they can't make ends meet, let alone us. But I don't understand who is living a good life!"

"I heard what Lao San said in the teahouse, the price of rice is cheap because too much foreign rice is imported. The harvest is not bad, why import so much foreign rice? It's really鬼! Liu Duo, are you talking about the rent collectors? They collect much less money, so naturally they feel苦了, they are used to good food and use. But they can get by as long as they use a little less, like us, that's…"

"Yesterday the price of rice was seven yuan and a half. If you weren't so impatient, I would have waited a day or two. Maybe it would have risen a little."

That one shook his head, making a face of disagreement, still coughing.

Both of them were silent, only the sound of the rudder splashing water, softly and rhythmically.

The boat entered the city river and slowed down. Many boats selling vegetables and firewood were blocking the way, which was very troublesome. Qiu Tang had no time to cough and was busy using the bamboo pole to hold back other people's boats, for fear of collisions. But his heart was beating non-stop, worrying about whether the price of rice would fall again today, and whether Wang Daye would be willing to give him a little more discount.

The large characters on the walls of several rice shops could already be seen vaguely. He felt like a prisoner about to be executed, and he had no idea in his mind. He looked back at Liu Duo, who was also frowning.

"Qiu Tang, why are you so slow?"

Seven or eight rice boats were parked in front of the rice shop, and two of them had not yet unloaded the rice.

"We set off late, what's wrong today?"

That one said angrily: "Seven yuan and two!"

"Seven yuan and two?" Qiu Tang and Liu Duo were both stunned.

"What's there to say? Pay the rent and go home and wait to starve to death!"

Liu Duo looked at Qiu Tang, put down the rudder, and sighed.

Small Notes from a Traveler's Window

— Shu

I.

Yu Xuanji's poem says: "It is easy to find priceless treasures, but hard to find a loving man"; Chen Meigong's poem says: "Ashamed to accept an insincere scholar, would rather associate with a sincere thief"; the former is spoken by someone who deeply understands the joys and sorrows of love, the latter is a cynical remark; in feudal society, it is rare to be able to talk so boldly.

II.

Yuan Zhonglang's "Hengtang Lang" poem is romantic and elegant, and is most widely recited. But what I have seen are two different versions. One of them is:

Hengtang crossing, the gentleman comes from the west, the lady goes to the east. I am grateful for the gentleman's great generosity. My home is in Hongqiao, at the crossroads of the Zhumen. Recognize the Magnolia denudata, do not pass the willow tree.

This is what I knew several years ago, and it seems that Xie Wuliang's "General History of Chinese Literature" quoted this one. This year I bought Zhonglang's Complete Works, and the version contained therein is quite different from the previous version. The poem says:

Hengtang crossing, walking by the water, the gentleman comes from the west, the lady goes to the east. I am not a singer's family member, but a woman from a large family in Honglou. I accidentally spat on the gentleman while blowing flowers, I am grateful for the gentleman's great generosity. My home is in Hongqiao, at the crossroads of the Zhumen. Recognize the Magnolia denudata, do not pass the Yumberry tree.

Both poems have their advantages, and I don't know if the former was revised by Zhonglang.

Two Brothers (46)

— By Maupassant, translated by Li Weike

He hoped that he might not see her before starting, and not plant on her cheeks the kiss that already disgusted him.

But she replied:

"Wait a bit, I am coming to open the door for you. But you must wait until I am back in bed before you come in."

He heard her bare feet upon the boards, then the shooting of the bolt. She called out:

"Come in."

He entered. She was sitting in bed, Roland beside her, his head wrapped in a handkerchief, turned to the wall, sound asleep. Nothing could wake him if someone did not shake him or pull him up. Those days that he went fishing, it was the sailor Babaguli who came at the appointed time and rang the bell to waken the servant girl, and then it was the servant girl who would drag her master from this profound sleep.

Pierre, as he went towards his mother, glancing at her, suddenly felt as if he had never possessed her.

She presented him with her cheeks, he kissed her lightly, then sat down on a low chair.

"Was it last night that you decided to go and loaf at Trouville?" she said. "Yes, it was last night that I decided."

"Are you coming back to dinner?"

"I do not know yet. At any rate, you need not wait for me."

He scrutinized her with a curiosity that was absolutely amazing. This was his mother, this woman! From childhood, from the time that his eyes were able to distinguish things, he had seen this entire face, this smile, this voice so familiar, so intimate, and all of them suddenly struck him as so estranged, so different from what he had hitherto seen and heard. He now knew that he had loved her before, but had never scrutinized her. This was still she, and he knew all the minutest details of her face; but it was the first time that he clearly saw these minute details. As he gazed carefully at this beloved head with a feeling of uneasiness, she appeared to him different from what she had been before, in an aspect which he had never discovered.

He got up to go, then suddenly was overcome by the strong desire to know that had been gnawing at his heart ever since the previous evening.

"By the way, I remember that when we lived in Paris there was a small portrait of Maréchale in the drawing-room, was there not?"

She hesitated for a second or two, or at least he thought that she hesitated, then she said:

"Yes."

"Where has that portrait gone to?"

In his mind she might have answered him even quicker.

"That portrait . . . wait a bit . . . I cannot remember exactly . . . it is in my writing-table, perhaps."

"Would you mind finding it for me?"

"Yes, I shall look for it by and by. What do you want it for?"

"Oh! it is not for myself. I think that it would be best to give it to Jeanne, and it would please her."

"Yes. You are right, that is a good idea. I shall look for it when I get up."
